No elected or appointed officer or employee shall: 
(1)  Solicit or accept any gift directly or indirectly, whether in the form of money, loan, gratuity, favor, service, thing or promise, or any other form, under circumstances in which it can reasonably be inferred that the gift is intended to influence him in the performance of his official duties. Nothing herein shall preclude the solicitation or acceptance of lawful contributions for election campaigns; 
(2)  Disclose confidential information gained by reason of the person's office or position or use this information for personal gain or benefit of anyone; 
(3)  Engage in any business transaction or activity or have a financial interest, direct or indirect, which is incompatible with the proper discharge of the person's official duties or which may intend to impair the person's independence or judgment in the performance of official duties; 
(4)  Receive any compensation for his services as an officer or employee of the city from any source other than the city except as otherwise provided by ordinance; or 
(5)  Represent private interest in any action or proceeding against the interest of the city or appear in behalf of private interest before any agency. 
(Code 1983, § 1-7-22; Ord. of 7-10-1979)  
Sec. 2-357. - Disclosure of interest. 
Any elected or appointed officer or employee who possesses or acquires any interest as might reasonably tend to create a conflict with the public interest shall make a full disclosure in writing to the appointing authority or to the city council in case of a member of the council, at any time the conflict becomes apparent. The disclosure statements shall be made a matter of public record and filed with the clerk-treasurer. Any member of the council who knows such member has a personal private interest, direct or indirect, and any proposal before the council, shall disclose the interest in writing to the council. This disclosure shall be made a matter of public record prior to the taking of any vote on the proposal. 
(Code 1983, § 1-7-23; Ord. of 7-10-1979)  
Sec. 2-358. - Fair and equal treatment. 
No elected or appointed officer or employee shall use that person's official position to secure or grant special consideration, treatment, advantage, privilege or exemption to himself or to any person beyond that which is available to every other person. 
(Code 1983, § 1-7-24; Ord. of 7-10-1979)  
Sec. 2-359. - No future employment. 
No person who has served as an elected or appointed officer or employee of the city shall, within one year after termination of such service or employment, appear for compensation before any agency of the city, or receive compensation for any services rendered in behalf of any private interest in relation to any case, proceeding or application with respect to which the person was directly concerned or which was under the person's active consideration, or with respect to which knowledge or information was made available to the person during the period of service of employment. 
(Code 1983, § 1-7-25; Ord. of 7-10-1979)  
Sec. 2-360. - City council to be judge of qualifications. 
The city council shall be the judge of the election and qualifications of its members and the grounds for forfeiture of their office and for that purpose shall have power to subpoena witnesses, administer oaths and require the production of evidence. Any member charged with conduct constituting grounds for forfeiture of his office shall be entitled to a public hearing on demand. A notice of the hearing shall be published in one or more newspapers of general circulation within the city at least one week in advance of the hearing. 
(Code 1983, § 1-7-26; Ord. of 7-10-1979)  
Sec. 2-361. - Penalties and disciplinary action for violation. 
Failure to comply with this division, or any violation of the standards of conduct established in this division, shall be grounds for forfeiture of office, removal from office or employment, or other offices, of all officers and employees of the city. 
(Code 1983, § 1-7-27; Ord. of 7-10-1979)  
Chapter 4 - ALCOHOLIC BEVERAGES[1] 

Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference— State preemption of acts encompassed in Alcohol Beverage Control Act, S.C. Code 1976, § 61-6-4490; municipal police enforcement powers, S.C. Code 1976, § 61-6-4510; municipal court jurisdiction of certain alcohol offenses, S.C. Code 1976, § 61-6-4500. 
 
Sec. 4-1. - Open alcoholic beverage containers in public. 
It shall be unlawful to publicly possess an open container of beer, wine, ale, porter, malt liquor or other alcoholic beverage on a public street or in a vehicle on a public street within the incorporated limits of the city. 
Public possession and consumption of alcoholic beverages. It shall be unlawful for any person to possess an open container or to drink any spirituous malt, vinous, fermented, brewed or other type of beer or wine which contains alcohol and is used as a beverage on any street, highway, park or public place not lawfully licensed to sell such beverage. A lawful exemption of the aforementioned is during the hours and location of a special event that has been properly permitted by the city. 
(Code 1983, § 7-1-6; Ord. of 9-25-1978; Ord. of 1-10-1995; Ord. No. 8-2014, 11-12-2014)  
Sec. 4-2. - Hours for public consumption of alcoholic beverages. 
(a)  Between the hours of 2:00 a.m. and 7:00 a.m. on Mondays through Sundays upon the premises of any private or nonprofit club, any store, beer parlor or any other place of business or commercial establishment authorized or licensed by law to sell wine, ale, porter, beer, malt liquors, or other alcoholic beverages it shall be unlawful for: 
(1)  An owner, employee or person in charge thereof to sell, offer for sale, give away, barter or exchange or in any manner dispense or permit the consumption of any wine, ale, porter, beer, malt liquor, or other alcoholic beverages; and 
(2)  Any person to drink or possess in an open container any wine, ale, porter, beer, malt liquor, or other alcoholic beverages. 
(b)  The provisions of subsection (a) of this section shall not prohibit during the aforesaid hours the sale or possession in sealed containers of beer, ale, porter, wine or other malt liquors for consumption off the premises. 
(c)  Commercial establishments which allow for the on-premises consumption of beer, ale, porter. wine, malt liquors, or other alcoholic beverages shall be prohibited from operating between the hours 2:00 a.m. and 7:00 a.m. on Mondays through Sundays. 
(Code 1983, § 7-1-7; Ord. of 9-25-1978; Ord. No. 3-2016, 4-12-2016; Ord. No. 6-2016, 7-12-2016)  
Chapter 6 - ANIMALS[1] 

Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Federal law reference— "Service animal" defined for purposes of Americans with Disabilities Act, 28 CFR 36.104. 
State Law reference— Municipal authority to enact ordinances for care and control of dogs, cats, and other animals, S.C. Code 1976, § 47-3-20; municipal powers not limited by state laws, S.C. Code 1976, § 47-3-70; required annual inoculation of pets against rabies, S.C. Code 1976, § 47-5-60; notice to health department of animal suspected of rabies, S.C. Code 1976, § 47-5-80. 
 
Sec. 6-1. - Definitions. 
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this chapter, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Abandonment means a situation in which an owner of an animal or pet does not provide for humane disposal of the animal or pet, or transfer ownership to a responsible person, or who does not provide or arrange for adequate food, water, shelter and care. 
Animal control officers means the persons designated by the city police department as the enforcement officers of the provisions of this chapter. 
Animal shelter means any premises designated by the city council for the purpose of impoundment, care or destruction of animal or pets found in violation of this chapter. 
Animals means all domestic, domesticated or wild members of the animal kingdom, including birds, but not including man. 
At large means an animal which is off the property and/or premises of the owner or keeper and not under physical control by owner or keeper by means of a leash or similar physical restraining device. 
Dangerous dog means: 
(1)  A dog with a known propensity, tendency, or disposition to attack unprovoked, to cause injury, or to otherwise endanger the safety of human beings or domestic animals; 
(2)  A dog which attacks a human being or domestic animal without provocation; 
(3)  A dog owned or harbored primarily or in part for the purpose of dogfighting or a dog trained for dogfighting; and 
(4)  Trained guard or attack dogs. 
Division means the animal control division of the city police department. 
Impound means assumption of custody of an animal by a police officer or employee of the police department for detention in a pound or animal shelter. 
Owner means any person who has a property right in a pet or an animal, keeps or harbors a pet or an animal or who has it in his care or acts as its custodian, or permits a pet or animal to remain in or about any premises occupied by him. There shall be a rebuttal presumption that a person has a property right in an animal if that person keeps or harbors a pet or animal or has an animal in his care or acts as its custodian for 21 consecutive days. 
Pet means all mammals of the order carnivore, including dogs and cats. 
Restraint means when a pet or animal is on the premises of its owner or keeper or when a pet is accompanied by owner or keeper and is physically controlled by a leash or similar physical device. 
Spayed female means any female dog or cat which has been operated on to prevent conception. 
Vaccination against rabies means the injection subcutaneously, intramuscularly or otherwise, of anti-rabid vaccine as approved by the department of agriculture/veterinary biologics division, administered by a licensed veterinarian. 
(Code 1983, § 6-2-1; Ord. of 10-13-1992)  
Sec. 6-2. - Penalty. 
Any person found guilty of violating this chapter shall be subject to the fines, penalties and/or incarceration as in the court's discretion it deems proper. 
(Code 1983, § 6-2-7; Ord. of 10-13-1992)  
Sec. 6-3. - Keeping of certain animals—Prohibited. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to keep within the city limits any horse, mule, cow, gannet, swine, domestic fowl, goat or cattle of any description, except as provided for in section 6-4. 
(Code 1983, § 6-2-2; Ord. of 10-13-1992)  
Sec. 6-4. - Same—Exceptions. 
(a)  Any resident or property owner who keeps an animal described in section 6-3 on the effective date of the ordinance from which this chapter is derived shall be notified by a registered letter of the provisions of this chapter, and such property owner shall be given a period of 60 days to remove such animal so as to comply with the provisions of section 6-3. Failure to comply with the provisions of section 6-3 within 60 days from the receipt of the notice shall constitute a violation of this chapter, and each day thereafter shall constitute a separate offense. 
(b)  Any person who on the effective date of the ordinance from which this chapter is derived is in violation of this chapter may apply to the city council for permission to keep such animal or apply to city council for permission to keep such animal. Such application to city council shall include information as to the facilities for the proper and humane care and treatment of such animal, type of shelter provided for the animal, and method for maintaining the area in a sanitary manner so as to remove health hazards. 
(c)  The council shall judge each separate application, provided, however, that the stable area or primary living area of such animal is not within 105 feet of any building owned or occupied by persons other than the owner of the animal. 
(d)  Such permit may at any time be revoked by council, upon 30 days' notice, if the council determines, after providing the owner an opportunity for a hearing, that the conditions on which the permit was issued have been violated. 
(e)  It is the purpose and intent of this section that none of the animals described in section 6-3 shall be henceforth brought into the city or kept or maintained within the city except as provided in this section. 
(f)  It is the further intent of the city council that any existing use of land for the purpose of keeping said animals within city limits shall be discontinued upon the animal's death. 
(Code 1983, § 6-2-3; Ord. of 10-13-1992)  
Sec. 6-5. - Manner of keeping and maintaining animals. 
All animals shall be kept and maintained in such a manner as to not injure, interfere with or disturb the property, peace, comfort, health, safety, or general welfare of any person within the city. No animal shall be kept confined or tied by rope, chain or wire that is less than 12 feet in length and must allow pet access to shelter, food and water without becoming entangled. 
(Code 1983, § 6-2-4; Ord. of 10-13-1992)  
Sec. 6-6. - Cruelty to animals. 
Any act, omission or neglect whereby unjustified physical pain, suffering or death of an animal caused or permitted shall be cruelty to animals. Without limiting the generality of the foregoing, whoever does any of the following shall be guilty of cruelty to animals: 
(1)  Overloads, overdrives, overworks, tortures, torments, poisons, ill-treats, deprives of necessary sustenance, shelter or ventilation, inflicts unnecessary pain or suffering upon any animal or causes the same to be done; 
(2)  Drives or works an animal when it is unfit for labor; 
(3)  Abandons or fails to provide proper treatment for a maimed, diseased, disabled or infirm animal; 
(4)  Carries or causes an animal to be confined or cared in any vehicle, or otherwise, in an unnecessarily cruel manner; 
(5)  Knowingly or willfully authorizes or permits any animal to be abandoned or to unnecessary suffering, torture or cruelty of any kind; 
(6)  Exhibits, keeps or displays an animal without providing it with access to an area shaded from the sun; 
(7)  Causes, encourages or allows any animal to attack, fight or harm another animal either as owner or otherwise; or 
(8)  Robs or destroys nests of wild fowl or animal; 
provided, however, that nothing herein contained shall prevent the trapping and elimination of rats, mice, bugs or other household pests or, with prior written approval of the chief of police or his designated representative, the trapping or destruction of birds, squirrels or other animals on specific premises where they are inflicting damages or have become a health hazard. 
(Code 1983, § 6-2-5; Ord. of 10-13-1992)  
Sec. 6-7. - Bird sanctuary. 
The territory embraced within the city or the police jurisdiction thereof is hereby declared to be a bird sanctuary. It shall be unlawful to kill, maim, or injure any wild or migratory bird or to destroy or to rob or molest eggs or nests in breeding places of any birds. 
(Code 1983, § 6-2-6; Ord. of 10-13-1992)  
Sec. 6-8. - Guard dogs for business. 
Any business may keep a watchdog to protect the premises of that business during the hours it is closed. However, if the dog is allowed access to fenced outside or yard areas while not under direct control of its guardian, the fence must be at least six feet high to prevent small children from inadvertently getting into the area with the dog. In addition, signs with block-printed letters at least three inches high, with the statement "BEWARE—THIS PROPERTY IS GUARDED BY DOG," must be displayed on all sides of the property in easy visual access. 
(Code 1983, § 6-2-8; Ord. of 10-13-1992)  
Sec. 6-9. - Sanitation. 
(a)  It shall be unlawful for the owner of any animal to allow the accumulation of waste excretions from animals which are offensive by sight or odor to any neighbor. All owners shall be required to move and dispose of all waste in a sanitary manner. Where a complaint is received regarding this section, the animal control officer shall investigate the complaint within 48 hours and if, in his opinion, the complaint is found to be justified, he shall give written notice to the owner (if necessary via adult member of the household) to clean the premises within 24 hours. If, by the expiration of the allotted time, the premises have not been satisfactorily cleaned, the owner or his agent shall be issued a summons (citation) to appear in municipal court. 
(b)  It shall be unlawful for any owner, keeper or walker of any dog or cat to permit his dog or cat to discharge its excreta upon any public or private property except upon the property of the owner of the animal or upon the property of one who has assented thereto unless such owner, keeper, or walker immediately thereafter removes said animal's excreta from the public or private property in question. 
(Code 1983, § 6-2-9; Ord. of 10-13-1992; Ord. of 12-11-2001)  
Sec. 6-10. - Animals at large prohibited. 
(a)  It shall be unlawful for any dog to be at large in the city unless it has a chain, substantial rope, leash or leather thong securely attached to its collar. A responsible person must be in actual physical control of the animal through the above-mentioned leash, etc., at all times. 
(b)  It shall be the duty of any owner, possessor, or person who harbors or keeps any animal to confine such animal within the limits of his premises except as above stated. 
(c)  The minimum fine upon violation and conviction of this section shall be in accordance with section 6-2. 
(Code 1983, § 6-2-10; Ord. of 10-13-1992)  
Sec. 6-11. - Procedure upon person being bitten. 
Any animal who bites any person within the city limits shall be confined for a period of not less than ten days. This section applies to both vaccinated and unvaccinated animals. It shall be at the discretion of the animal control officer and/or the chief of police whether said animal shall be confined upon the owner's premises or placed in a private or county pound. If deemed necessary to place the animal in a private or county pound, all costs shall be the responsibility of the owner of the animal. 
(Code 1983, § 6-2-11; Ord. of 10-13-1992)  
Sec. 6-12. - Inspections and right of entry. 
Whenever it is necessary to conduct an investigation to enforce any of the provisions of or perform any duty imposed by this chapter, or other applicable law, or whenever the animal control officer or any authorized member of the department or a recognized humane society or SPCA or a volunteer animal control officer working under the police department has probable cause to believe that there exists in any building or upon any premises any violation of the provisions of this chapter or other applicable law in an emergency situation, the animal control officer or any police officer is hereby empowered to enter such property at any reasonable time and to inspect the same and perform any duty imposed upon the animal control officer or any police officer by this chapter or other applicable laws; if not an emergency situation, a search warrant must be obtained. 
(Code 1983, § 6-2-12; Ord. of 10-13-1992)  
Sec. 6-13. - Vaccination against rabies. 
(a)  No person shall own, keep, or harbor any pet within the city unless such pet has received, as evidenced by certificate, a vaccination from a licensed graduate veterinarian using a vaccine which is good for a period of one year, provided such vaccine has been approved with the longer period of time specified by the state department of health and environmental control after consolation with the executive committee of the state association of veterinarians. 
(b)  A state department of health and environmental control certificate of pet rabies vaccination will be issued by a licensed graduate veterinarian for each pet, stating the name and address of the owner, the name, breed, color and markings, age, sex of animal, and the veterinary or pharmaceutical control number of the vaccination. 
(c)  Coincident with the issuance of the certificate, the licensed graduate veterinarian shall also furnish a serially numbered metal tag bearing the same number and year as is on the certificate. The metal license tag shall bear the name of the veterinarian and shall at all times be attached to a collar or harness worn by the pet for which the certificate and tag have been issued. Tags must be of the same color and shape when issued in offices of veterinarians. 
(d)  The owner shall have a valid certificate of rabies vaccination readily available at all times for inspection by the animal control officer or the police department designee or health officials. 
(e)  In the event that a rabies tag is lost, the owner shall obtain a duplicate tag within seven working days. 
(f)  A certificate of rabies vaccination issued by a licensed veterinarian from another state will be accepted as valid evidence provided it is less than a year from date of issue. 
(g)  Rabies inoculation must be given by age four months to all cats and dogs. 
(Code 1983, § 6-2-13; Ord. of 10-13-1992)  
Sec. 6-14. - Enforcement of rabies control provisions of this chapter and state law; impoundment. 
The provisions of this chapter relating to control of rabies and the provisions of the Rabies Control Act (S.C. Code 1976, § 47-5-10 et seq.) shall be enforced by animal control officers. 
(1)  Animals found running at large in violation of S.C. Code 1976, § 46-5-130 (having no valid rabies inoculation tag) shall be impounded by the animal control officer and transferred to the SPCA, county pound or suitable humane facility. 
(2)  Animals impounded under the provisions of the Rabies Control Act (S.C. Code 1976, § 47-5-130) may be redeemed only as provided in S.C. Code 1976, § 47-5-140. The redeemer must show proof of current payment for rabies inoculation, and the redeemer must pay for daily boarding costs assessed by the animal shelter and a $25.00 pickup fee for the city. 
(Code 1983, § 6-2-14; Ord. of 10-13-1992)  
Sec. 6-15. - Impoundment of pets running at large; disposition. 
(a)  Any animal or dangerous animal running at large shall be impounded by the animal control officer or any of the persons empowered to enforce this chapter and held at the city or transported to the county animal shelter and there impounded and confined until redeemed or disposed of as hereinafter provided. 
(b)  Immediately after impounding any animal, the animal control officer shall make a reasonable effort to notify the owner in writing of its impoundment and to inform the owner of the conditions whereby he can regain custody of the animal. 
(c)  Animals not claimed by their owners after notification or attempted notification, or before the expiration of seven days, shall become the property of the animal shelter and shall be euthanized in a manner prescribed in S.C. Code 1976, § 47-3-410 et seq., or placed for adoption through an approved animal shelter or private humane association. 
(d)  Any animal determined by the animal control officer to be abandoned shall be impounded by the animal control officer and transferred to an approved animal shelter or private humane association. 
(Code 1983, § 6-2-15; Ord. of 10-13-1992)  
Sec. 6-16. - Redemption from impoundment. 
(a)  The owner shall be entitled to resume possession of an animal impounded under section 6-15 upon compliance with the rabies vaccination requirement, proper identification, and the payment of redemption fees herein set forth. 
(b)  The owner of an impounded animal must apply for the redemption of this animal. The animal may not be released unless authorized by the animal control officer or police officer with assurance from the owner that proper care or custody will be maintained. 
(c)  Redemption fees. The fees set forth herein shall be as determined from time to time by ordinance. 
(d)  It shall be unlawful for any person to release from impoundment without proper authority any animal or to resist animal control officers engaged in the impoundment of any animal. 
(Code 1983, § 6-2-16; Ord. of 10-13-1992)  
Sec. 6-17. - Impoundment of animals without proper care due to incapacity or involuntary absence of owner; abandonment. 
Whenever the animal control officer or a police officer finds that any animal is or will be without proper care because of injury, illness, incarceration or other involuntary absence of the person responsible for the care of such animal, such officer may impound such animal and place it with the SPCA, county pound or other approved private humane organization until reclaimed by its owner. The owner must pay the applicable fees in the same manner as any other owner would redeem an impounded animal prior to the release of such animal. Any animal which has been impounded and not reclaimed for ten days after the circumstances causing the impoundment have ceased to exist, may be adopted out immediately after the expiration of ten days from the time of impounding without the posting of any notice whatsoever. 
(Code 1983, § 6-2-17; Ord. of 10-13-1992)  
Sec. 6-18. - Animal care. 
(a)  No person or those owning or having possession, charge, custody or control of any animal shall cause or fail to provide said animal with sufficient good and wholesome food, clean water, proper shelter, care and veterinary treatment when needed. 
(b)  An animal control officer shall cause a citation to be issued if there is probable cause to believe that any of the following events has occurred: 
(1)  Abandonment an animal, or cause an animal to be abandoned, including abandoning any dog, cat or other domesticated animal in any public place including the rights-of-way of any public highway, road, street or on the property of another; 
(2)  An animal has been knowingly exposed to any poisonous substance, whether mixed with food or not, so that the same shall be in a manner to be eaten by an animal, fish, bird, fowl or reptile, provided that it shall not be unlawful for a person to expose on his own property common rat poison mixed only with vegetable substances; 
(3)  An animal has been beaten excessively or cruelly, ill treated, tormented, tortured, overloaded, overworked, or otherwise abused, or any fight or other combat between animals, or an animal and a human, has been caused, instigated or permitted; 
(4)  An operator of a vehicle has struck an animal, immediately reports such injury or death to the appropriate authorities; in the event the owner cannot be ascertained or found, such operator shall at once report the accident to the animal control officer or police; 
(5)  Any live animal, fish, bird, fowl or reptile has been given away as a prize for or as an inducement to enter any contest, game or other competition, or as an inducement to enter a place of amusement or offer such species as an incentive to enter into any business agreement whereby the offer was for the purpose of attracting trade; 
(6)  An animal's ears or tail has been cropped, notched or split by someone other than a licensed veterinarian; 
(7)  A person has failed to provide medical treatment or has denied medical treatment for any diseased, sick or injured animal; 
(8)  A person has failed to provide or has denied necessary sustenance, such as food or adequate amounts of food and water to sustain flesh or permit normal growth, or has provided an inadequate amount of clean water or water that is sour, filthy or spoiled; 
(9)  A person has failed to remove excrement and maintain the shelter of a confinement area in a clean, odor-free condition; and free of ticks, fleas, flies or mosquitoes; 
(10)  A person has teased, baited or in any manner molested any animal not belonging to him or legally under his control; 
(11)  A person has failed to provide or has denied shelter for any animal, fish, bird, fowl or reptile of any kind in any manner without shading same from the sun, any direct light, heat or cold and providing adequate ventilation for their use; and 
(12)  A person or owner who, through negligence, has let his animals run free, break loose, or escape in any manner. 
(Code 1983, § 6-2-18; Ord. of 10-13-1992)  
Sec. 6-19. - Number of pets. 
(a)  It shall be unlawful to own and keep more than three male or female cats and three male or female dogs over the age of four months. 
(b)  Anyone violating subsection (a) of this section shall have the excess animals given to a new home. 
(c)  If corrective action is not taken after notice from the animal control officer, the animal control officer will remove the excess animals to the county pound or other humane facility. 
(Code 1983, § 6-2-19; Ord. of 10-13-1992)  
Sec. 6-20. - Adoption. 
(a)  Any animal impounded under the provisions of this chapter may, at the end of the legal detention periods, have its title transferred to the county animal shelter or SPCA or be adopted by a person deemed to be a responsible and suitable owner, who will agree to comply with the provisions of this chapter. All required fees must be paid at the time of adoption. 
(b)  If at the end of the seven days' retention period the animal has not been reclaimed by its owner, it shall be considered eligible for adoption. To encourage adoption of animals, the adopter will be required to pay only the daily boarding fee for the initial seven-day retention period of $14.00. The adopter shall also complete an application for adoption which shall include a declaration of his intention to have the animal inoculated against rabies. When the application is properly completed and the fees paid, the animal shall be released to be adopted. Animals shall be considered adoptable if they are in good health and are not vicious. The city reserves the right to have a representative inspect the premises of a prospective adopter and may refuse the applicant if the accommodations do not meet the standards set forth in section 6-9. 
(c)  No animal over three months of age shall be released or adopted until prepayment is made for vaccination against rabies. 
(Code 1983, § 6-2-20; Ord. of 10-13-1992)  
Sec. 6-21. - Restraining and pets which disturb the peace. 
(a)  It shall be unlawful for any owner or custodian of any pet or animal to permit same to run at large at any time upon streets or highways or properties other than his own property within the city. 
(b)  It shall be unlawful for the owner of any animal to allow the animal to become a nuisance to any other resident. The following shall be deemed a public nuisance: 
(1)  Continuous, untimely barking, molesting passersby, chasing vehicles (motored or otherwise). 
(2)  Trespassing on public property. 
(3)  Trespassing on private property or attacking other domestic animals by an animal. 
(c)  Any animal found roaming at large will be picked up by the animal control officer and may be picked up by any police officer or other designated agent and taken to the animal impoundment facilities or restrained for pickup by the animal control officer. Any animal found trespassing on the private property of a resident or property owner may be humanely restrained by the resident or property owner pending notification to and pickup by the animal control officer. 
(d)  Every female dog or cat in heat shall be confined in a building or secure enclosure in such a manner that such female dog or cat cannot come in contact with another animal except for planned breeding. 
(e)  No owner of any pet shall allow his pet by reason of frequent or continual noise to disturb the peace of neighbors. 
(f)  It shall be unlawful to keep a dangerous dog in any manner not allowed under S.C. Code 1976, § 47-3-710 et seq. 
(g)  Violation of this section will be subject to penalties of section 6-2 (S.C. Code 1976, § 47-3-710 et seq.). 
(Code 1983, § 6-2-21; Ord. of 10-13-1992)  
Sec. 6-22. - Regulation of dangerous dogs. 
(a)  No person owning or harboring or having the care or the custody of a dangerous dog may permit the dog to go unconfined. Such dog must be securely confined indoors or confined in a securely enclosed and locked pen or dog-run with sides of at least six feet with a secure top. If the pen or structure has no bottom secured to the sides, all sides must be embedded. However, the provisions of this section shall not apply to any dog that is owned by a licensed security company and is on patrol in a confined area. 
(b)  No person owning or harboring or having the care of a dangerous dog may permit the dog to go beyond his premises unless the dog is securely muzzled and restrained with a chain having a minimum tensile strength of 300 pounds and not exceeding three feet in length. 
(c)  Dogfighting; offering for sale. 
(1)  No person may own or harbor a dog for the purpose of dogfighting or train, torment, badger, bait or use a dog for the purpose of causing or encouraging the dog to unprovoked attacks upon human beings or domestic animals. 
(2)  No person may possess with intent to sell, offer for sale, breed, or buy or attempt to buy a dangerous dog. 
(d)  Seizure and impoundment. 
(1)  In the event a law enforcement agent has probable cause to believe that a dangerous dog is being harbored or cared for in violation of this section, he may petition the city judge having jurisdiction to order the seizure and impoundment of the dangerous dog while the trial is pending. 
(2)  In the event a law enforcement agent has probable cause to believe that a dangerous dog is being harbored or housed in violation of this section, he may with proper court petition seize and impound the dangerous dog while the trial is pending. 
(3)  Penalties. 
a.  Whoever violates this section is guilty of a misdemeanor and, upon conviction, for a first offense, must be fined not more than $200.00 and or imprisoned for not more than 30 days. 
b.  A dangerous dog which attacks a human being or another domestic animal may be ordered destroyed when in the court's judgment the dangerous dog represents a continuing threat of serious harm to human beings or other domestic animals. 
c.  Any person found guilty of violating this section shall pay all expenses, including shelter, food, veterinary expenses for boarding and veterinary expenses, necessitated by the seizure of any dog for the protection of the public or other expenses as may be required for the destruction of the dog. Furthermore, anyone found guilty of violating this section shall pay any medical expenses incurred by the victim as a result of the attack by a dangerous dog. 
(e)  Owner's premises. 
(1)  A person is lawfully upon the premises of the owner within the meaning of this section when he is on the premises in the performance of any duty imposed upon him by the laws of this state, by the laws or postal regulations of the United States, when he is on the premises upon invitation, expressed or implied, of the owner, or when he is in the performance of a duty relative to public safety, which includes police officer, firefighter or other authorized personnel. A person has the right to ingress and to egress from the premises for any purpose connected with the performance of the public safety duty. 
(2)  A person who is lawfully on the owner's premises and who is attacked by a dangerous dog or witnesses the attack may use reasonable force to repel the attack. A person is not liable in damages or otherwise for action to repel or any action taken to restrain or control a dog from an unprovoked attack. 
(3)  The chief of police, in exigent or emergency circumstances, may cause a dangerous animal to be slain or removed from the city. 
(Code 1983, § 6-2-22; Ord. of 10-13-1992)  
Sec. 6-23. - Duties of animal control division. 
The police department's division of animal control shall be charged with the responsibility of: 
(1)  Cooperating with the health offices of the various state government units and assisting in the enforcement of the laws of the state with regard to the control of animals, and especially with regard to the vaccination of dogs and cats against rabies; 
(2)  Investigating all complaints with regard to animals covered by this chapter; 
(3)  Enforcing within the city all of the state laws, ordinances enacted by the city, and contracts entered into by the city for the care, control and custody of animals covered by this chapter; 
(4)  Supervising and being in charge of animals impounded in the holding facility, until such time as ownership of such animals is given to the appropriate animal shelter; 
(5)  Enforcing provisions of state law regarding dangerous dogs (S.C. Code 1976, § 47-3-710 et seq.). 
(Code 1983, § 6-2-23; Ord. of 10-13-1992)  
Sec. 6-24. - Division members as peace officers; badges. 
Each member of the animal control division, while performing his duties, shall wear a uniform and carry an identification card identifying him as an animal control officer of the city. 
(Code 1983, § 6-2-24; Ord. of 10-13-1992; Ord. of 9-13-2005, § 1)  
Sec. 6-25. - Trapping; steel traps. 
(a)  It shall be unlawful for any person to trap any form of wildlife without the written consent of the animal control officer. 
(b)  It shall be unlawful for any person to use any type of steel traps, snares or other trapping devices which are known to cause bodily injury to animals. 
(Code 1983, § 6-2-25; Ord. of 10-13-1992)  
Sec. 6-26. - Notice of violation; procedure; punishment. 
In discharging their duties under this chapter, the animal control officer and police officers are hereby empowered to issue a citation to any person if there is probable cause to believe that he has violated any of the provisions of this chapter. Any citation so issued may be delivered in person to the alleged violator by the animal control officer or any member of the police department or it may be mailed, certified, return receipt requested, to the person so charged, if he cannot be readily found. Any notice or citation so delivered or mailed shall direct the alleged violator to appear at a municipal court on a specific day and hour named in the notice, or pay a fine in lieu of appearing in court. 
(Code 1983, § 6-2-26; Ord. of 10-13-1992)  
Chapter 8 - BUILDINGS AND BUILDING REGULATIONS[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference— Enforcement of building codes by local governments, S.C. Code 1976, § 6-9-10; codes applicable to building inspections, S.C. Code 1976, § 6-9-130; building codes amendment procedure, S.C. Code Reg. 8-240; qualifications for building codes amendments, S.C. Code Reg. 8-245; local adoption of building codes, S.C. Code Reg. 8-265; municipality may not enforce national building code provisions regulating farm structures, S.C. Code 1976, § 6-9-65(B); municipal responsibility to enforce barrier-free building design standards, S.C. Code Reg. 19-400.3(B). 
 
ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 
 
Sec. 8-1. - Fire limits designated. 
The fire limits are established as being such territory or portion as designated "general commercial" on the official zoning map of the city. 
(Code 1983, § 5-1-1) 
State Law reference— Establishing fire limits, S.C. Code 1976, § 5-25-1110.  
Sec. 8-2. - Violations and penalties. 
Any person who shall violate a provision of this chapter, or fail to comply therewith, or with any of the requirements thereof, or who shall erect, construct, alter, demolish, or move any structure, or has erected, constructed, altered, repaired, moved or demolished a building or structure in violation of a detailed statement or drawing submitted and approved thereunder shall be guilty of a misdemeanor. Each such person shall be deemed guilty of a separate offense for each and every day or portion thereof during which any violation of any of the provisions of this chapter is committed, or continued and, upon conviction of any violation, the person shall be subject to a penalty as provided in section 1-12. Nothing therein contained shall prevent the city from taking any other lawful action as is necessary to prevent or remedy any violation of this chapter. 
(Code 1983, § 5-1-90; Ord. of 7-14-1975)  
Secs. 8-3—8-20. - Reserved.  
ARTICLE II. - BUILDING CODE 
 
Sec. 8-21. - International Building Code adopted. 
For the purpose of establishing rules and regulations for the construction and removal of buildings or other structures, or any appurtenances connected or attached thereto, there is hereby adopted the International Building Code, with subsequent revisions and appendices D, E, F, I, and J thereto, as published by the International Code Council, Inc., a copy of which has been and is now filed in the office of the clerk-treasurer and is hereby adopted and incorporated by reference as fully as if set out at length herein and the provisions of which shall be controlling as to all subjects therein contained, within the corporate limits of the city, except that in the event that any of the provisions of the building code are in conflict with other provisions of this Code, state law, or ordinances, rules or regulations, the provisions of this Code, state law or ordinances, rules or regulations shall prevail and be controlling. 
(Code 1983, § 5-1-2; Ord. of 6-5-1984; Ord. of 2-14-1989; Ord. of 11-8-1994; Ord. of 10-10-1995; Ord. of 6-12-2001)  
Sec. 8-22. - Administration. 
(a)  Definitions. The following words, terms and phrases, when used in the International Building Code, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this subsection, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Department of law means the city attorney. 
(b)  Smoke detectors required. Every existing dwelling, mobile home and every dwelling unit within an apartment house, condominium, townhouse and every guestroom in a motel or hotel, every sleeping room in dormitories and every basement or cellar within such dwellings shall be provided with an approved smoke detector, installed in accordance with the manufacturer's recommendation and listing. When activated, the detector shall provide an audible alarm. The smoke detectors shall be tested in accordance with the manufacturer's recommendation and listing. When activated, the detector shall provide an audible alarm. The smoke detectors shall be tested in accordance with and meet the requirements of UI 217, Single and Multi Station Smoke Detectors. 
(Code 1983, § 5-1-3; Ord. of 6-12-2001)  
Sec. 8-23. - International Residential One- and Two-Family Building Code adopted. 
For the purpose of erecting, fabrication, construction, enlargement, alteration, repair, location and use of detached one and two family dwellings, their appurtenances and accessory structures, there is hereby adopted the International Residential One- and Two-Family Building Code, and all appendices and revisions, except D, F, I, and K published by the International Code Council, Inc., and the whole thereof except the portions as are hereafter deleted, modified or amended, a copy of which has been and is now filed in the office of the building official, and which is hereby adopted and incorporated by reference as fully as if set out at length herein and the provisions thereof shall be controlling as to all subjects herein contained, within the corporate limits, except that in the event that any of the provisions of the residential code are in conflict with other provisions of this Code, state law, or ordinances, rules or regulations, the provisions of this Code, state law, or regulations shall prevail and be controlling. 
(Code 1983, § 5-1-4; Ord. of 6-11-2002)  
Sec. 8-24. - Fees and penalties. 
(a)  The fee amounts and fines concerning building permits, inspections, moving fees, demolition fees, and temporary electrical poles are established from time to time by ordinance. 
(b)  Where work for which a permit is required by this Code is started or proceeded prior to obtaining such permit, the fees herein specified shall be doubled, but the payment of such double fee shall not relieve any persons from fully complying with the requirements of this Code in the execution of this work nor from any other penalties prescribed herein. When additional inspections are required for reason of deficient or defective work, or otherwise through fault or error on the part of the permit holder or on the part of his employees, after receiving notice in writing by the inspector setting forth the violation. Only one such inspection shall be made under the regular fees as herein prescribed, in building, mechanical, plumbing, gas, electrical and mobile homes, and for any additional inspection required. 
(c)  When the valuation of the proposed construction exceeds $1,000.00 and a plan is required to be submitted, a plan-checking fee shall be paid to the building official at the time of submitting plans and specifications for checking. Such plan-checking fee shall be equal to one-half of the building permit fee as set forth in subsection (a) of this section. Such plan-checking fee is in addition to the building permit fee. 
(Code 1983, § 5-1-5; Ord. of 6-12-2001; Ord. of 4-9-2002)  
Secs. 8-25—8-51. - Reserved.  
ARTICLE III. - ELECTRICAL CODE 
 
Sec. 8-52. - National Electrical Code adopted. 
The National Electrical Code, as recommended by the National Fire Protection Association, is adopted as the minimum standard for the installation of all electrical wiring, devices and equipment in the city, and is made a part of this article as fully and to the same extent as if copied herein in full. A copy of the electrical code is on file in the office of the building official. In the event of any conflict between the provisions of the electrical code and the provisions of this Code, state law or ordinances, rules and regulations, the provisions of this Code, state law or ordinances, rules or regulations shall prevail and be controlling. 
(Code 1983, § 5-1-11; Ord. of 6-5-1984; Ord. of 2-14-1989; Ord. of 1-9-1990; Ord. of 11-8-1994; Ord. of 10-10-1995; Ord. of 6-12-2001)  
Sec. 8-53. - Administration and enforcement of article provisions. 
The provisions of this article shall be administered and enforced by the building official. 
(Code 1983, § 5-1-12)  
Sec. 8-54. - Service connection, disconnection and installation. 
(a)  For all service entrances (S.E. cables) for electrical services which penetrate exterior walls of any commercial and industrial structure, an outside fused disconnect will be required. 
(b)  For all service entrances (S.E. cables) for electrical services which penetrate exterior walls of any residential structure, an outside fused disconnect will be required on all services 400 amps or more, and/or for those electrical services of 400 amps or less, in lieu of an outside disconnect, may penetrate the exterior wall with a minimum schedule 40 conduit (electrical) from the meter can to main disconnect. 
(c)  Service upgrades and those structures that have had their power off for a period exceeding six months will be required to meet the minimum safety requirements of the installation of GFCI (ground fault) circuits and disconnects at mechanical (heating and air conditioning) equipment. 
(Code 1983, § 5-1-13; Ord. of 6-12-2001)  
Sec. 8-55. - Electrical wiring, plumbing, etc., not to be lathed or sealed prior to inspection and posting of notices. 
It shall be unlawful to lathe, seal or in any manner conceal any electrical wiring, plumbing, or equipment until it has been inspected by the inspector, and notices posted that the work is satisfactory. 
(Code 1983, § 5-1-14; Ord. of 7-14-1975)  
Sec. 8-56. - Approval of electrical devices, materials and appliances. 
All electrical devices, materials or appliances designed for attachment or installation on any electrical circuit or system for light, heat or power shall not be sold, offered for sale, installed or used unless they shall be approved by the Underwriter's Laboratory, Inc. 
(Code 1983, § 5-1-15; Ord. of 7-14-1975)  
Sec. 8-57. - Permit fees. 
Any person making application for a permit for the installation or alterations or maintenance of electrical wiring, devices, appliances and/or equipment shall pay to the city a fee as established from time to time by resolution of the city council. 
(Code 1983, § 5-1-16; Ord. of 6-5-1984; Ord. of 4-9-2002(1); Ord. of 4-9-2002(2))  
Secs. 8-58—8-87. - Reserved.  
ARTICLE IV. - PLUMBING CODE 
 
Sec. 8-88. - International Plumbing Code adopted. 
The International Plumbing Code, and appendices A, B, D, E and F thereof, together with all subsequent revisions thereto published by the International Code Council, Inc., is hereby adopted as the minimum standard relating to the installation of all plumbing, including the pipes for distributing the water supply, the fixtures for using water and sewage, together with fittings and appurtenances of various kinds, all within or adjacent to the buildings within the city or where connected to the city's sewerage system, and the whole thereof is incorporated herein as fully as if set out at length, and all plumbers shall be required to make installations in conformity with the plumbing code and the regulations contained therein, a copy of which is on file in the office of the clerk-treasurer. In the event of any conflict between the provisions of the plumbing code and the provisions of this Code, state law or ordinances, rules or regulations, the provisions of this Code, state law or ordinances, rules or regulations shall prevail and be controlling. 
(Code 1983, § 5-1-31; Ord. of 6-5-1984; Ord. of 2-14-1989; Ord. of 11-8-1994; Ord. of 10-10-1995; Ord. of 6-12-2001)  
Sec. 8-89. - Administration. 
(a)  Definitions. The following words, terms and phrases, when used in the International Plumbing Code, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this subsection, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Administrative authority and local governing body means the council. 
Department of law means the city attorney. 
Plumbing inspection department means the building official. 
Plumbing official means the building official. 
(b)  Pipe cleanouts. A pipe cleanout shall be installed at the property line and should be no more than 12 inches below grade with the access opening at grade level. 
(Code 1983, § 5-1-32; Ord. of 6-12-2001)  
Secs. 8-90—8-106. - Reserved.  
ARTICLE V. - GAS CODE 
 
Sec. 8-107. - International Fuel Gas Code adopted. 
The International Fuel Gas Code and appendices A, B, C, and D thereto, with all subsequent revisions, which fuel gas code is published by the International Code Council, Inc., and which is referred to, incorporated herein, and made a part hereof for all purposes, and a copy of which is on file in the office of the clerk-treasurer, is hereby adopted. In the event of any conflict between the provisions of the fuel gas code and any provision of this Code, state law or ordinances, rules or regulations, the provisions of this Code, state law or ordinances, rules or regulations shall prevail and be controlling. 
(Code 1983, § 5-1-41; Ord. of 6-12-2001)  
Sec. 8-108. - Administration. 
Any person, company, or contractor shall be required to be licensed for performance of any kind of construction, reconstruction, alteration, repair or other work upon any property for gas piping within the city. A license is also required for any public utility corporation subject to regulations by the duly constituted authorities of the public service commission. Permits shall be secured and such work shall be inspected as provided in the International Fuel Gas Code adopted by this article. 
(Code 1983, § 5-1-42; Ord. of 6-12-2001)  
Sec. 8-109. - Administration, enforcement of article provisions. 
The provisions of this article shall be administered and enforced by the building official. 
(Code 1983, § 5-1-43)  
Sec. 8-110. - Scope, effect of provisions. 
This article shall not be construed to relieve from or lessen the responsibility of any party owning, operating, controlling or installing any gas piping or gas appliances from damages to anyone injured thereby, nor shall the city be held as assuming any liability by reason of inspection authorized herein, or certificate issued. 
(Code 1983, § 5-1-44)  
Secs. 8-111—8-133. - Reserved.  
ARTICLE VI. - MECHANICAL CODE 
 
Sec. 8-134. - International Mechanical Code adopted. 
The International Mechanical Code and appendices A and B thereto, with all subsequent revisions, published by the International Code Council, is adopted as the mechanical code of the city to provide basic code requirements governing the safe installation and maintenance of all mechanical equipment so as to safeguard life, health and public welfare and the protection of property, and each of the regulations, provisions, penalties, conditions and terms of such mechanical code is hereby referred to, adopted and made a part of this article. 
(Code 1983, § 5-1-51; Ord. of 6-5-1984; Ord. of 2-14-1989; Ord. of 11-8-1994; Ord. of 6-12-2001)  
Sec. 8-135. - Administration. 
(a)  Definitions. The following words, terms and phrases, when used in the International Mechanical Code, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this subsection, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Mechanical inspection department means the building official. 
Mechanical official means the building official. 
(b)  Right of appeal. The right of appeal provided in the mechanical code shall be to the board of examiners and review. 
(Code 1983, § 5-1-52; Ord. of 6-12-2001)  
Secs. 8-136—8-153. - Reserved.  
ARTICLE VII. - PROPERTY MAINTENANCE CODE 
 
Sec. 8-154. - International Property Maintenance Code adopted. 
The International Property Maintenance Code, as published by the International Code Council, Inc., is hereby adopted. Such property maintenance code is incorporated herein and made a part hereof for all purposes, a copy of which is filed for record in the office of the clerk-treasurer, and the provisions of such property maintenance code shall be controlling in the use, maintenance and occupancy of all dwellings, dwelling units and/or structures within the city. In the event of any conflict between the provisions of the property maintenance code and the provisions of this Code, state law or ordinances, rules or regulations, the provisions of this Code, state law or ordinances, rules or regulations shall prevail and be controlling. 
(Code 1983, § 5-1-61; Ord. of 6-12-2001)  
Secs. 8-155—8-178. - Reserved.  
ARTICLE VIII. - ENERGY CONSERVATION 
 
Sec. 8-179. - International Energy Conservation Code adopted. 
The International Energy Conservation Code, as published by the International Code Council, Inc., is hereby adopted. Such energy conservation code is incorporated herein and made a part hereof for all purposes, a copy of which is filed for record in the office of the clerk-treasurer, and the provisions of such energy conservation code shall be controlling in the use, maintenance and occupancy of all dwellings, dwelling units and/or structures within the city. In the event of any conflict between the provisions of the energy conservation code and the provisions of this Code, state law or ordinances, rules or regulations, the provisions of this Code, state law or ordinances, rules or regulations shall prevail and be controlling. 
(Code 1983, § 5-1-71; Ord. of 6-12-2001)  
Secs. 8-180—8-196. - Reserved.  
ARTICLE IX. - PERMITS AND INSPECTIONS 
 
Sec. 8-197. - Permits required. 
No building construction, reconstruction, alteration or repairs; no swimming pool construction, reconstruction, alteration or repairs; no electrical construction, reconstruction, alteration or repairs; no mechanical construction, reconstruction, alteration or repairs; and no gas construction, reconstruction, alteration or repairs, unless it is metered gas, shall be installed within or on any building, structure or premises without first securing a permit therefor from the building official or his assistants authorized to issue such permits. Applications for permits shall be made on forms provided for this purpose by the building official. 
(Code 1983, § 5-1-81; Ord. of 7-14-1975)  
Sec. 8-198. - Annual permits. 
(a)  Annual permits may be issued to firms employing a full-time engineering department and professionally supervised maintenance force. An annual permit shall entitle the firm to undertake repair and construction projects on its own buildings relating to operation and maintenance and to process related construction, alteration or modification without securing permits required in section 8-197. The firm shall be required to submit an annual report of any projects completed to the building official with an affidavit from the plant engineer or underwriter or approved inspection agency that all work has been done in accordance with the standard building code. The firm to which an annual permit is issued shall be entitled to such reasonable inspections as may be requested by the officer of said company. Annual permits shall expire on December 31 of the year in which they were issued. 
(b)  An annual permit may be issued to property managers for performance of normal maintenance on rental property provided that no single repair job exceeds the sum of $500.00; provided further, however, that should any electrical or plumbing repairs be made by the manager a regular permit must be obtained inasmuch as such electrical and plumbing repairs shall not be covered by the blanket permit. Annual permits shall expire on December 31 of the year in which they were issued. 
(Code 1983, § 5-1-82; Ord. of 7-14-1975)  
Sec. 8-199. - Limitation. 
An unprocessed application for a permit for any proposed work shall be deemed to have been abandoned six months after the date of filing. 
(Code 1983, § 5-1-83; Ord. of 7-14-1975)  
Sec. 8-200. - Examination of drawings. 
The building official shall examine or cause to be examined each application for permit and the drawings and computations filed therewith and shall ascertain by such examinations whether the construction or alteration indicated and described is in accordance with the requirements of this chapter and all other pertinent laws or ordinances. 
(Code 1983, § 5-1-84; Ord. of 7-14-1975)  
Sec. 8-201. - Action on application. 
(a)  No owner, firm, corporation, authorized agent, or contractor shall construct, enlarge, alter, repair, move, demolish or change the occupancy of a building or structure, or to erect, install, enlarge, alter, repair, remove, convert or replace any electrical, gas, mechanical, or plumbing system, the installation of which is regulated by the technical codes, or to cause any such work to be done, shall first make application to the building official and obtain the required permit for the work. 
(b)  If the work described in an application for permit and the drawings filed therewith conform to the requirements of this chapter and other pertinent laws and ordinances, the building official shall issue a permit therefor to the applicant. 
(c)  If the application for a permit and the drawings filed therewith describe work which does not conform to the requirements of this chapter, or other pertinent laws or ordinances, the building official shall not issue a permit, but shall return the drawings to the applicant with his refusal to issue the permit. This refusal shall, when requested, be in writing and shall contain the reasons therefor. 
(Code 1983, § 5-1-85; Ord. of 7-14-1975; Ord. of 11-8-1994)  
Sec. 8-202. - Conditions of the permit. 
The building official shall act upon an application for a permit with plans as filed, or as amended, without unreasonable or unnecessary delay, but no later than seven days after application is filed. A permit issued shall be construed to be a license to proceed with the work and shall not be construed as authority to violate, cancel, alter, or set aside any of the provisions of this chapter, nor shall the issuance of a permit prevent the building official thereafter requiring a correction of errors in plans or in construction, or of violations of this chapter. Every permit issued shall become invalid unless the work authorized by the permit is commenced within six months after its issuance, or if the work authorized by the permit is suspended or abandoned for a period of six months after the time the work is commenced; provided that, for cause, one or more extensions of time, for periods not exceeding 90 days each, may be allowed in writing by the building official. 
(Code 1983, § 5-1-86; Ord. of 7-14-1975)  
Sec. 8-203. - Failure to obtain a permit. 
(a)  If any person commences any work on a building or structure before obtaining the necessary permit from the building official, he shall be subject to the penalty described in section 8-2. 
(b)  Where construction is commenced before a permit is obtained, the permit fees shall be doubled. 
(Code 1983, § 5-1-87; Ord. of 7-14-1975)  
Sec. 8-204. - Table of construction values; grounds for refusal of permits. 
The building official is authorized to establish a table of values, which shall reflect the average cost of construction, and in the event that an application for a building permit reflects a figure which appears to be underestimated on the application, the permit shall be denied, unless the applicant can show detailed estimated cost to meet the approval of the building official. Permit valuations shall include total cost, such as plumbing, electrical, mechanical and other systems. 
(Code 1983, § 5-1-88; Ord. of 7-14-1975)  
Sec. 8-205. - Permit to be kept at site; inspection. 
The permit when issued shall be kept at the building or place where the construction, erection, improvements or alteration is being done and on demand shall be produced by the person in charge of the work for inspection by any police officer, the inspector, or any member of the city council or city administrator, and it shall be unlawful to continue the work after such demand unless and until the permit is produced for the inspection. 
(Code 1983, § 5-1-89; Ord. of 7-14-1975)  
Sec. 8-206. - Construction, installation or maintenance by homeowner. 
Nothing in this chapter shall prevent any homeowner from constructing, installing or repairing within his own property boundaries, providing the work is done by himself and is used exclusively by him or his family. This privilege does not convey the right to violate any of the provisions of this chapter, nor is it to be construed as exempting any property owner from obtaining a permit and paying the required fees therefor. 
(Code 1983, § 5-1-91; Ord. of 7-14-1975)  
Sec. 8-207. - Notice to inspector that work is ready for inspection. 
When the building, swimming pool, electrical, mechanical, gas or other work in any building or structure for which a permit has been obtained is ready for inspection, notice shall be provided to the inspector stating the location of work, the name of the owner and the name of the contractor. 
(Code 1983, § 5-1-92; Ord. of 7-14-1975)  
Sec. 8-208. - Notice for final inspection; certificate of inspection. 
After the entire completion of the work, a notice, the same as in section 8-207, shall be given to the inspector for the final inspection, and if he finds the work has been satisfactorily done, he shall issue a certificate of inspection. This certificate does not relieve the contractor of his responsibility for any defective work which may have escaped the notice of the inspector. 
(Code 1983, § 5-1-93; Ord. of 7-14-1975)  
Sec. 8-209. - Permit not required. 
The building official shall not require permits for: 
(1)  The replacement of lamps; 
(2)  The connection of portable devices to suitable receptacles which have been permanently installed; 
(3)  The installation, alteration or repair of wiring, devices, appliances or equipment for the operation of signals or the transmission of intelligence where such wiring, devices, appliances or equipment operate at a voltage not exceeding 50 volts between conductors and do not include generating or transmitting equipment capable of supplying more than 100 watts; or 
(4)  Public service corporations for the installation of equipment necessary in the generation, transmission and distribution of electric energy. 
(Code 1983, § 5-1-94; Ord. of 7-14-1975)  
Sec. 8-210. - Requirement of licenses; work by owner; public utilities; equipment with automatic controls. 
(a)  This article shall not require a license for performance of any kind of electrical wiring installation upon any property: 
(1)  By the owner thereof, or by employees of the owner, or members of the family of the owner; 
(2)  By or for public utility corporations subject to regulation by the duly constituted authorities of the public service commission, and where such property is required as a part of the plant of the corporation and is so utilized in rendering its service to the public; or 
(3)  By or for mechanical contractors installing equipment with automatic controls and requiring interwiring. Permits shall be secured, however, and all such work shall be inspected as provided within this chapter. 
(b)  The phrase "by employees of the owner," as used in this section, shall not be construed to include any contractor employed by the owner; nor shall the wording in this section be interpreted so as to abrogate or in any way modify the permit, inspection, or any other sections and provisions of this chapter; nor shall the relief from licensing provided by this section apply to a builder, developer, or contractor engaged in the construction of buildings for resale. 
(Code 1983, § 5-1-95; Ord. of 7-14-1975)  
Sec. 8-211. - Certificate of approval; notice to utility. 
(a)  After each required inspection, a notice shall be given to the permit holder as to approval or disapproval, with a listing of required corrections if any are required. Electrical wiring shall not be covered or concealed until after the work has been approved; inspection must be made by the inspector within 24 hours of request for inspection by the contractor, unless the request should come after 10:00 a.m. on a Friday or the day before a holiday. If the notice indicated that corrections are needed, the corrections shall be made forthwith and the inspector notified and inspection requested. 
(b)  Upon final inspection of the electrical wiring and in compliance with the electrical code of the city, a certificate of approval, if required, will be issued immediately to the permit holder; also a permanent release, if required, shall be issued to the utility notifying them of the approval. It shall be unlawful for any person to connect or reconnect any installation until a certificate of approval authorizing the connection has been issued. 
(Code 1983, § 5-1-96; Ord. of 7-14-1975)  
Sec. 8-212. - Fees. 
Any person making application for a permit for the construction, reconstruction, alteration or repairs of buildings, appurtenant structures, swimming pools, electrical, plumbing, mechanical, gas or for any other work for which a permit is required shall pay to the city a fee in such amount as fixed from time to time by the council. 
(Code 1983, § 5-1-97; Ord. of 7-14-1975)  
Secs. 8-213—8-234. - Reserved.  
ARTICLE X. - BUILDING OFFICIAL 
 
Sec. 8-235. - Appointment; term. 
There shall be appointed by the council, with the advice of the city administrator, an officer of the city who shall be designated the building official, and who shall serve at the pleasure of the council. 
(Code 1983, § 5-1-111)  
Sec. 8-236. - Duties. 
The building official shall be charged with the general supervision of all construction in the city and shall report to the chief of the fire department any infraction of the fire code. He shall assist any of the officials of the city in ascertaining all factual data useful to their consideration of matters coming before them. He shall meet with the board of examiners and review in all matters, but shall have no vote. The building official shall perform any other functions and duties as may be prescribed in this chapter, any ordinance of the city, any regulation adopted by the city council, or under state law or assigned to him by the city administrator. 
(Code 1983, § 5-1-112; Ord. of 7-14-1975)  
Sec. 8-237. - Office of inspector created; building official as inspector. 
There is hereby created the office of inspector for the city. The building official shall be the inspector. For the purpose of this chapter, the inspector shall be the building, housing, swimming pool, electrical, plumbing, mechanical and gas inspector, unless some other person is appointed by the council to perform the duties of such office. 
(Code 1983, § 5-1-113; Ord. of 7-14-1975)  
Sec. 8-238. - Deputy. 
The city administrator may designate as a deputy for the inspector an employee of the city who shall, during the absence or disability of the inspector, exercise all of the powers of the inspector. 
(Code 1983, § 5-1-114; Ord. of 7-14-1975)  
Sec. 8-239. - Records, annual report and summary. 
The inspector shall keep or cause to be kept a record of the business of the division. The division records shall be open to the public. The inspector shall annually submit a report to the city administrator, covering the work of the division during the preceding year. He shall incorporate in this report a summary of appeals to and decisions of the board of examiners and review. 
(Code 1983, § 5-1-115; Ord. of 7-14-1975)  
Sec. 8-240. - Right of entry. 
The inspector shall enforce the provisions of this chapter, and he, or his duly authorized representative, may enter any building, structure, or premises for just and proper cause, at any reasonable time and with reasonable prior notice to perform any duty imposed upon him by this chapter, except that no entry shall be made into occupied residences between 6:00 p.m. and 6:00 a.m. unless permission shall have been granted by the occupant prior to the hour of 6:00 p.m. most immediately preceding. 
(Code 1983, § 5-1-116; Ord. of 7-14-1975)  
Sec. 8-241. - Stop work orders. 
Upon notice from the inspector that work on any building or structure is being done contrary to the provisions of this chapter, or in a dangerous or unsafe manner, such work shall be immediately stopped. This notice shall be in writing and shall be given to the owner of the property or to his agent, or to the person doing the work, and shall state the conditions under which work may be resumed. The inspector shall have the authority to refuse any permits for future work to be done by such contractors. Where an emergency exits, no written notice shall be required. 
(Code 1983, § 5-1-117; Ord. of 7-14-1975)  
Sec. 8-242. - Revocation of permits. 
The inspector may revoke a permit or approval issued under the provisions of this chapter in case there has been any false statement or misrepresentation as to material fact in the application or plan on which the permit or approval was based. 
(Code 1983, § 5-1-118; Ord. of 7-14-1975)  
Sec. 8-243. - Tests. 
The inspector may require tests or test reports as proof of compliance. Tests, if required, are to be made at the expense of the owner or his agent by an approved testing laboratory or other approved agency. Copies of the test reports or the results of all tests shall be kept on file in the office of the inspector. 
(Code 1983, § 5-1-119; Ord. of 7-14-1975)  
Sec. 8-244. - Unsafe buildings. 
All buildings or structures which are unsafe, unsanitary, or not provided with adequate egress, or which constitute a fire hazard, or are otherwise dangerous to human life, or which in relation to existing use constitute a hazard to safety or health by reason of inadequate maintenance, dilapidation, obsolescence, or abandonment, are severally in contemplation of this section, unsafe buildings. All unsafe buildings are hereby declared illegal and shall be abated by repair and rehabilitation or by demolition in accordance with the following procedure: 
(1)  Whenever the inspector shall find any building or structure or portion thereof to be unsafe, he shall, in accordance with established procedure for legal notices, give the owner, agent, or person in control of the building or structure written notice stating the defects thereof. This notice shall require the owner within a stated time either to complete specified repairs or improvements, or to demolish and remove the building or structure or portion thereof. 
(2)  If necessary, the notice shall also require the building, structure or portion thereof to be vacated forthwith and not reoccupied until the specified repairs and improvements are completed, inspected and approved by the inspector. The inspector shall cause to be posted at each entrance to the building a notice stating: 
"THIS BUILDING IS UNSAFE AND ITS USE OR OCCUPANCY HAS BEEN PROHIBITED BY THE BUILDING OFFICIAL." 
This notice shall remain posted until the required repairs are made or demolition is completed. It shall be unlawful for any person or his agents, or other servants, to remove the notice without written permission of the inspector, or for any person to enter the building except for the purpose of making the required repairs or of demolishing same. 
(3)  The owner, agent or person in control shall have the right, except in cases of emergency, to appeal from the decision of the inspector, as provided hereinafter, and to appear before the board of examiners and review at a specified time and place to show cause why he should not comply with the notice. 
(4)  In case the owner, agent, or person in control cannot be found within the stated time limit, or, if the owner, agent or person in control shall fail, neglect, or refuse to comply with notice to repair, rehabilitate, or to demolish and remove the building or structure or portion thereof, the inspector, after having ascertained the cost, shall cause the building or structure or portion thereof, to be demolished, secured, or required to remain vacant. 
(5)  The decision of the inspector shall be final in cases of emergency which, in his opinion, involve imminent danger to human life or health. He shall promptly cause any building, structure, or portion thereof to be made safe or cause its removal. For this purpose, he may at once enter any structure or land on which it stands, or abutting land or structures, which any assistance and at any cost as he may deem necessary. He may order the vacation of adjacent structures and may require the protection of the public by appropriate fence or other means as may be necessary, and for this purpose may close a public or private way. 
(6)  Costs incurred under this section shall be charged to the owner of the premises involved and shall be collected in the manner provided by law. 
(Code 1983, § 5-1-120; Ord. of 7-14-1975)  
Sec. 8-245. - Requirements not covered by chapter. 
Any requirement necessary for the strength or stability of an existing or proposed building or structure, or for the safety or health of the occupants thereof, not specifically covered by this chapter, shall be determined by the inspector, subject to appeal to the board of examiners and review. 
(Code 1983, § 5-1-121; Ord. of 7-14-1975)  
Sec. 8-246. - Alternate materials and alternate methods of construction. 
The provisions of this chapter are not intended to prevent the use of any material, or method of construction not specifically prescribed by this chapter, provided any alternate has been approved and its use authorized by the inspector. The inspector shall approve any alternate, provided he finds that the proposed design is satisfactory and complies with the provisions of this chapter, and that the material, method, or work offered is, for the purpose intended, at least the equivalent of that prescribed in the code in quality, strength, effectiveness, fire resistance, durability, and safety. The inspector shall require that sufficient evidence or proof be submitted to substantiate any claim that may be made regarding its use. If, in the opinion of the inspector, the evidence and proof are not sufficient to justify approval, the applicant may refer the entire matter to the board of examiners and review. 
(Code 1983, § 5-1-122; Ord. of 7-14-1975)  
Sec. 8-247. - Restrictions on employees. 
No officer or employee connected with the department, except one whose only connection is as a member of the board of examiners and review, shall be financially interested in the furnishing of labor, material, or appliances for the construction, alteration, or maintenance of a building, or in the making of plans or of specifications therefor, unless he is the owner of the building. No officer or employee shall engage in any work which is inconsistent with his duties or with the interests of the department. 
(Code 1983, § 5-1-123; Ord. of 7-14-1975)  
Sec. 8-248. - Liability. 
No officer or employee or member of the board of examiners and review charged with the enforcement of his duties shall thereby render himself liable personally, and he is hereby relieved from all personal liability for any damage that may accrue to person or property as a result of any act required or permitted in the discharge of his duties. Any suit brought against any officer or employee because of any act performed by him in the enforcement of any provision of this chapter shall be defended by the city attorney until the final termination of the proceedings. 
(Code 1983, § 5-1-124; Ord. of 7-14-1975)  
Sec. 8-249. - Hardships. 
Where the literal application of the requirements of this chapter would appear to cause undue hardship on an owner or tenant or when it is claimed that the true intent and meaning of this chapter or any of the regulations therein have been misconstrued or wrongly interpreted, the owner of the building or structure, or his duly authorized agent, may appeal from the decision of the inspector to the board of examiners and review. 
(Code 1983, § 5-1-125; Ord. of 7-14-1975)  
Sec. 8-250. - Appeal from decision of inspector. 
It is the intention of this chapter that all questions arising in connection with the enforcement of this code shall be presented first to the inspector and that any questions shall be presented to the board of examiners and review only on appeal from the decision of the inspector. 
(Code 1983, § 5-1-126; Ord. of 7-14-1975)  
Secs. 8-251—8-278. - Reserved.  
ARTICLE XI. - BOARD OF EXAMINERS AND REVIEW 
 
Sec. 8-279. - Created; membership. 
(a)  There is hereby created by the council a board, referred to in all standard codes as the board of adjustment and appeals, to be known as the board of examiners and review, which shall consist of seven members appointed by city council. The members shall be residents of the city and shall be closely related to the building industry. One member shall be a registered professional engineer and/or architect, if available. Members of this board shall be appointed for three-year terms. 
(b)  Any one or more members of the board shall be subject to removal or replacement by the council at any time for stated cause after a public hearing, if requested. Vacancies shall be filled for an unexpired term in the manner in which the original appointments are required to be made. The members of the board shall serve without compensation. 
(c)  The board shall hold an annual organizational meeting in March to elect a chairman, vice-chairman and secretary for a one-year term. These officers of the board may succeed themselves in consecutive terms.
