In addition, it is the intent and purpose of the city council to protect and further the rights of residents who desire to receive door-to-door solicitation or canvassing at all times. 
Recognizing that political and religious canvassing and/or solicitation is a Constitutional right, nothing herein shall limit or constrict the rights of a political candidate, political campaign worker, or church representative from communicating with the public about their cause. 
(b)  Definitions. 
Soliciting shall mean and include any one or more of the following activities: 
(1)  Seeking to obtain orders for the purchase of goods, wares, merchandise, foodstuffs, services of any kind, character or description whatever for any kind of consideration whatever; or 
(2)  Seeking to obtain prospective customers for application or purchase of insurance of any type, kind or publication; or 
(3)  Seeking to obtain subscriptions to books, magazines, periodicals, newspapers and every other type or kind of publication; or 
(4)  Seeking to obtain gifts or contributions of money, clothing or any other valuable thing for the support or benefit of any charitable or nonprofit association, organization, corporation or project. 
(c)  Duty of solicitor. It shall be the duty of every solicitor or canvasser, commercial or noncommercial, upon going into a neighborhood or residential address to look for any signs that would preclude solicitation. Further, upon entering any premises in the city on which a residence is located to proceed from the adjacent road right-of-way directly toward the front or main entrance of such residence to examine and look for the notice provided for in paragraph (d) herein. 
If any such notice is posted, then any solicitor or canvasser shall immediately and peacefully depart from the premises or neighborhood, as applicable, and shall leave on the premises no documents or literature of any kind. Under no circumstances shall a solicitor enter upon a side or rear yard of any residence unless expressly invited to do so by the occupant thereof. 
Any solicitor or canvasser who has gained entrance to any residence, whether invited or not, shall immediately and peacefully depart from the premises when requested to do so by an occupant or owner hereof. 
(d)  Declaration. It is hereby declared to be unlawful and shall constitute a trespass for any person to: 
(1)  Go upon any premises and ring the doorbell upon or near any door or create any sound in any manner calculated to attract the attention of the occupant of such residence for the purpose of securing an audience with the occupant thereof and engaged in soliciting or canvassing commercially or noncommercially in defiance of the notice exhibited at the residence in accordance with the provisions of this section. 
(2)  Not immediately and peacefully depart from the premises when requested to do so by an occupant or owner thereof. 
(e)  Notice to solicitor. 
(1)  When a homeowners association (HOA) or private residence owner or occupant does not wish to receive door-to-door solicitation or canvassing, a sign shall be posted at the entrance to the community, if an HOA, or in the immediate vicinity of the front door or front door bell area, which sign shall read: 
NO SOLICITATION INVITED 
or 
NO SOLICITING 
(2)  The signs provided for in subsection (1) shall be made of a durable material, such as plastic, metal or wood. Further, the sign letters shall be at least three-quarter inch in height. In addition, the sign shall be capable of being temporarily or permanently affixed to the hanging surface. 
(3)  Penalties. Any person, corporation or business entity violating any of the provisions of this section shall, upon conviction thereof, be subject to a fine of not more than $1,093.00 fine or 30 days imprisonment. 
(Ord. No. 7-2013, 7-9-2013)  
Secs. 26-67—26-88. - Reserved.  
ARTICLE IV. - OFFENSES AGAINST PROPERTY 
 
Sec. 26-89. - Petit larceny. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to commit the crime of petit larceny, as defined under state law, within the corporate limits of the city. 
(Code 1983, § 9-4-1) 
State Law reference— Petit larceny prohibited, S.C. Code 1976, § 16-13-30.  
Sec. 26-90. - Damaging property. 
Any person who shall injure any animal or the property of another, or who shall damage any goods, wares or merchandise, or other personal property of another person or any public property, if the property or animal has a value of $1,000.00 or less, shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor. Any person who shall damage or destroy any fencing, fences, trees, shrubbery or buildings on the land of another or belonging to any other person shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor. 
(Code 1983, § 9-4-2)  
Sec. 26-91. - Removing, destroying, or leaving down fences. 
Any person other than the owner who shall remove, destroy or leave down any portion of any fence intended to enclose animals of any kind, crops or uncultivated lands or who shall leave open any gate or leave down any bars or other structure intended for a like purpose shall be guilty of a misdemeanor. 
(Code 1983, § 9-4-3)  
Sec. 26-92. - Altering and removing landmarks. 
If any person shall knowingly, willfully, maliciously or fraudulently cut, fell, alter or remove any certain boundary tree or other allowed landmark, lamppost, lamp, or shade tree, the person so offending shall be guilty of a misdemeanor. 
(Code 1983, § 9-4-4)  
Sec. 26-93. - Intefering with, obstructing or improperly using drains and ditches. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to obstruct any of the drains or ditches within the city by depositing therein any dirt, trash, refuse or other matter. It shall also be unlawful for any person to empty into these ditches and drains any filth, garbage or sewage or to construct anything on, over, or contiguous to such ditches and drains in such manner that the construction shall or may thereafter constitute an obstruction or tend to obstruct the ditches and drains or in any manner interfere with keeping and maintaining the ditches and drains, unless a permit first is secured from the city administrator in writing, approving the nature, form and extent of the construction. 
(Code 1983, § 9-4-5; Ord. of 5-13-1974)  
Sec. 26-94. - Entry upon railroad rights-of-way or property prohibited. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to enter or be upon any railroad right-of-way without the express consent of the company owning such right-of-way or property; provided, however, that the prohibition of this section shall not apply to entry or presence on any publicly maintained grade crossing. 
(Code 1983, § 9-4-6; Ord. of 8-9-1983)  
Chapter 28 - PLANNING, LAND USE AND DEVELOPMENT  
ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 
 
Secs. 28-1—28-18. - Reserved.  
ARTICLE II. - PLANNING COMMISSION[1] 

Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference— Local planning commission, S.C. Code 1976, § 6-29-310 et seq. 
 
Sec. 28-19. - Establishment; purpose. 
In order to guide and accomplish a coordinated and harmonious development of the area which will, in accordance with existing and future needs, best promote the public health, safety, morals, order, convenience, prosperity, and the general welfare, as well as efficiency and economy in the process of development, the Hanahan Planning Commission, hereinafter referred to as the planning commission, is hereby established. 
(Code 1983, § 5-2-1; Ord. of 10-8-1973)  
Sec. 28-20. - Membership; term; compensation. 
The planning commission shall consist of seven members to be appointed by the city council. Members shall serve four-year staggered terms. Any vacancy in membership shall be filled for the unexpired term by the city council which shall also have the authority to remove any member for cause, on written charges, after a public hearing. All members shall serve without compensation but may be reimbursed for actual expenses incurred in connection with their official duties. 
(Code 1983, § 5-2-2; Ord. of 10-8-1973; Ord. of 4-13-2004)  
Sec. 28-21. - Organization; meetings; rules; staff; finances. 
The planning commission shall elect a chairperson and vice-chairperson from among its members. The term of the chairperson and other officers shall be one year with eligibility for reelection. The commission shall appoint a secretary who may be an officer or an employee of the city council or of the planning commission. The planning commission shall adopt rules for the transaction of business and shall keep a record of its recommendations, transactions, findings and determinations; and shall meet at the call of the chairperson and at such times as the chairperson or commission may determine. All meetings of the planning commission at which official action is taken shall be open to the public and all records of the commission shall be a public record. The commission may appoint any employees and staff as it may deem necessary for its work and may make expenditures for salaries of any employees and staff, contracts with consultants, and for the purchase of required equipment and supplies. The expenditures of the commission, exclusive of gifts, shall be within the amounts appropriated for this purpose by the city council. 
(Code 1983, § 5-2-3; Ord. of 10-8-1973)  
Sec. 28-22. - Powers and duties. 
(a)  From and after the time when the planning commission shall have organized and selected its officers and shall have adopted its rules of procedure, the commission shall have all the powers, duties and responsibilities set forth by state law. 
(b)  In general, the planning commission shall have the power to: 
(1)  Prepare and revise periodically a comprehensive plan and program for the development of its jurisdiction; 
(2)  Prepare and recommend for adoption to the appropriate governing authority as a means for implementing the plan and program: 
a.  Zoning ordinances or resolutions, and maps and appropriate revisions thereof for its jurisdiction; 
b.  Regulations for the subdivision of land and appropriate revisions thereof within its jurisdiction, and to administer the regulations that may be adopted; 
c.  An official map and appropriate revision thereof showing the exact location of existing or proposed public street, highway and utility rights-of-way and public building sites, together with regulations to control the erection of buildings or other structures or changes in land use within such rights-of-way, building sites or open spaces within its political jurisdiction or a specified portion thereof; and 
d.  A capital program for its jurisdiction based on the comprehensive plan and the capital improvements necessary to implement the plan. Such a capital program shall include an annual capital budget based on estimates of the cost of proposed projects and the means of financing them. The commission shall submit the capital program, including the capital budget, to the governing authority as directed; 
(3)  Establish principles and policies for guiding action in the development of the area; 
(4)  Prepare and recommend to the city council for adoption ordinances promoting orderly development in accordance with the comprehensive plan; 
(5)  Determine whether specific proposed developments conform to the principles and requirements of the comprehensive plan for the growth and improvement of the area; 
(6)  Review and recommend to the city council any needed changes in the zoning ordinance and the official zoning map, as well as the subdivision regulations, official map, other codes, ordinances, and controls related to the city's development; and 
(7)  Keep the city council and the general public informed and advised as to the matters described in this section. 
(Code 1983, § 5-2-4; Ord. of 10-8-1973)  
Secs. 28-23—28-47. - Reserved.  
ARTICLE III. - SUBDIVISIONS 
 
Sec. 28-48. - Ordinance incorporated by reference. 
The subdivision ordinance of the city, adopted November 4, 1975, as amended, are hereby incorporated herein and made a part of this Code by reference. Copies of the subdivision ordinance are on file in the office of the clerk-treasurer. 
(Code 1983, § 5-3-1)  
Secs. 28-49—28-69. - Reserved.

Footnotes:

Federal law references— Preservation of local zoning authority concerning wireless telecommunications facilities, 47 USC 322(c)(7); limited federal preemption of state and local zoning laws affecting amateur radio facilities, Memorandum Opinion and Order, PRB-1, 101 FCC 2d 952 (1985) and 47 CFR 97.15(b); Religious Land Use and Institutionalized Persons Act, 42 USC 2000cc et seq. 
State Law reference— Zoning ordinances and purposes, S.C. Code 1976, § 6-29-710; zoning districts, S.C. Code 1976, § 6-29-720; board of zoning appeals, S.C. Code 1976, § 6-29-780. 
 
Sec. 28-70. - Ordinance incorporated by reference. 
The zoning ordinance of the city, adopted November 12, 1973, as now or hereafter amended, is hereby incorporated herein and made a part of this Code by reference. Copies of the zoning ordinance are on file in the office of the clerk-treasurer. 
(Code 1983, § 5-4-1)  
Chapter 30 - SIGNS  
ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 
 
Secs. 30-1—30-18. - Reserved.  
ARTICLE II. - POLITICAL SIGNS 
 
Sec. 30-19. - Prohibited; exception. 
No sign shall be erected within the corporate limits of the city for the purpose of identifying, supporting, or advertising in any form or fashion persons, positions of persons, or any party or organization seeking election to a public office except as specifically provided for in, and in compliance with, chapter 8, section 8.8 of the City of Hanahan Zoning Ordinance. 
(Code 1983, § 5-6-21; Ord. of 8-14-1978; Ord. No. 6-2014, 8-13-2014)  
Chapter 32 - SOLID WASTE[1] 

Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference— Solid waste management and storage, transportation and collection of municipal solid wastes, S.C. Code Reg. 61-107.5; full cost disclosure by local governments concerning solid waste management, S.C. Code 1976, § 44-96-90. 
 
Sec. 32-1. - Definitions. 
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this chapter, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Brown trash means furniture items such as sofas, chairs, TVs, mattresses, carpeting/padding, etc. 
Business means any commercial operation, church, school, governmental or nonprofit organization or residential sites with more than two units on any common property. 
Common property means any lot, lot record, lot of record, property, tract, or property under common ownership which is used for a single purpose whichever term encompasses the larger unit of land. 
Garbage means normal household waste, including kitchen waste, organic waste matter, both animal and vegetable, small cans, bottles, clothing, rags, boxes, paper and any other similar waste. 
Residence means single-family units and any other residential unit with no more than two units on any lot. 
White goods means metal items such as appliances, metal furniture, wire or pipe, free of nonmetal materials, which can be safely accommodated by city personnel and equipment. 
Yard trash means all ashes, leaves, grass, bushes, vines, tree branches with no piece exceeding four inches in diameter and four feet in length, or other vegetation normally found outside the home. 
(Code 1983, § 3-2-1; Ord. of 12-10-1996, § I; Ord. of 10-14-1997; Ord. of 9-27-2000; Ord. of 9-14-2004, § I)  
Sec. 32-2. - Penalties. 
(a)  Every person failing to comply with this chapter will be subject to a fine of not more than $500.00 or imprisonment for not more than 30 days. Each day of violation shall constitute a separate offense. The city shall have the authority to refuse collection services for failure to comply with the rules of this chapter. Designated personnel from the public works department shall be authorized to enforce this chapter. Specific violations shall be as follows: 
(1)  Improper household solid waste containerization. 
(2)  Failure to properly handle excess household waste. 
(3)  Uncover household containers. 
(4)  Failure to follow prescribed curbside practices. 
(5)  Litter or unsightly growth on private or public property. 
(6)  Accumulation of litter at construction or residential sites. 
(b)  The penalty for the violations in subsection (a) of this section shall be a fine not to exceed $500.00. 
(Code 1983, § 3-2-9; Ord. of 12-10-1996, § IX; Ord. of 9-27-2000)  
Sec. 32-3. - Prohibited waste. 
(a)  Discarded building materials, lumber, shingles, rocks, bricks, concrete, etc., or dead animals shall not be deposited for garbage collection. These items shall be disposed of by the property owner. 
(b)  Tree removal. The removal of entire trees exceeding four-inch trunk diameter shall not be placed at the curb for collection. Property owners will be responsible for removal of all materials (i.e., limbs, trunks, stumps, etc.). 
(c)  No tires, lead-acid batteries, oil or auto parts of any kind will be collected by the city. Disposal shall be the responsibility of the owner, individual, or individuals in possession of the same. 
(d)  Contractors' and builders' refuse, bricks, scraps of lumber, mortar, plaster, roofing, guttering, shavings, tree debris, and all other like materials generated by a contractor during new construction, renovations, demolition, etc., shall be removed by the contractor, owner or tenant of the premises, each being jointly and severally responsible for such removal and transported to the county construction, demolition and land clearing debris landfill. 
(e)  Materials generated by residents or businesses as a result of salvage operations shall be the responsibility of the generator for removal and disposal (i.e., white goods, tires, electronics, lawnmowers, etc.). 
(f)  No waste classified and identified by the department of health and environmental control as hazardous waste shall be collected by the city. 
(g)  The city shall not assume responsibility for the collection of any materials left behind by tenants. Disposal shall be the responsibility of property owners. 
(h)  Any materials deemed by the city to pose a hazard to collection personnel or equipment shall not be collected. 
(Code 1983, § 3-2-2; Ord. of 12-10-1996, § II; Ord. of 9-27-2000; Ord. of 9-14-2004, § II)  
Sec. 32-4. - Liquids prohibited. 
All garbage and refuse shall be drained of liquid before being deposited for collection. 
(Code 1983, § 3-2-3; Ord. of 12-10-1996, § III; Ord. of 9-27-2000; Ord. of 9-14-2004, § III)  
Sec. 32-5. - Throwing waste from elevated places prohibited. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to throw, let fall or permit to drop from windows, roofs, porches or other elevated places any dirty water, garbage, ashes, paper, or other unclean useless waste material where this act may damage or affect surrounding property. 
(Code 1983, § 3-2-4; Ord. of 12-10-1996, § IV; Ord. of 9-27-2000; Ord. of 9-14-2004, § IV)  
Sec. 32-6. - Refuse collection. 
(a)  White goods, pieces of metal and tin, which can be safely accommodated by city personnel and equipment and which is placed at the curb by the resident shall be collected by the city on designated days. For purposes of this section, the term "white goods" shall include refrigerators, stoves, washing machines, dryers, water heaters, window air conditions, and such other items as may be added from time to time by the public works director. Metals other than white goods may not exceed four feet in length and two feet in width and 25 pounds in weight. For the safety of all, it shall be the responsibility of the resident to remove the doors from all refrigerators and freezers. The city will transport all white goods containing Freon in a manner which ensures against accidental discharge of Freon. 
(b)  All leaves, grass clippings and all other small yard waste shall be placed in biodegradable paper bags, not exceeding 65 pounds, at the curb on designated days. It shall be the responsibility of the resident to provide the necessary bags. Loose leaves, grass clippings and other small yard waste placed at the curb in piles, boxes or bags other than biodegradable paper bags, not exceeding 65 pounds, will not be collected. Loose leaves and grass may be placed in the approved city-issued 96-gallon cart, or 32-gallon trash cans with lids. No household garbage or other materials will be mixed with leaves or grass. Home composting of leaves and grass is encouraged for all residents. 
(c)  Limbs, brush, hedge and shrub trimmings, and all like materials may be placed at the curb in unbagged piles for collection subject to the following conditions: 
(1)  Piles of unbagged yard debris must be placed near the curb in an orderly manner, allowing city equipment and personnel reasonable access. 
(2)  The length of material shall be limited to four feet. 
(3)  The diameter of the material shall be limited to four inches. 
(4)  Materials must be compatible with city collection methods and equipment. 
(5)  No materials, as listed in this section, generated by contractors, landscapers, residential remodeling, lot clearing/preparation, etc., shall be collected by the city. 
(6)  Each resident shall be entitled to the collection of three cubic yards of unbagged yard waste per scheduled collection. Unbagged yard waste in excess of three cubic yards shall not be placed on the street until the following week of collection. 
(d)  Brown trash, including furniture, mattresses, tires, carpeting/padding, and other dry bulk items placed at the curb by the resident, shall be collected by the city on designated days subject to the following conditions: 
(1)  No hazardous materials shall be collected by the city. 
(2)  No shingles or building materials shall be collected by the city. 
(3)  No bricks, rocks, sand, concrete, mortar, etc., shall be collected by the city. 
(4)  Large items such as couches or chairs shall be placed near the curb, but safely out of the roadway. 
(5)  Carpeting/padding must be bundled and secured with length not exceeding five feet in diameter and weighing no more than 75 pounds. 
(6)  These items may not be placed on the curb prior to 8:00 a.m. of the day previous to the day of collection. 
(e)  Material shall not be placed on top of water meters, driveways, adjacent to fire hydrants, mailboxes, drainage ditches, stormwater intakes, on top of sprinkler heads, or close to any object or material that may be damaged by mechanical loading devices. Damage to such hidden objects or properties in the course of collection shall be the responsibility of the property owner. 
(f)  Collection of materials listed in subsections (a) through (d) of this section shall be subject to the following additional conditions: 
(1)  Items in each of the four categories must be separated and placed within six feet of the curb in such a way as to allow for easy access from the street by collection crews. If different categories of waste are mixed together, the material shall not be collected by the city. It shall be the owner's or resident's responsibility to separate these materials at the curb. 
(2)  Collection days shall be identified and scheduled by the city. Every effort will be made to notify all residents of collection days and any changes in collection days. 
(3)  Routes and schedules shall be designated and published by the city. 
(Code 1983, § 3-2-5; Ord. of 12-10-1996, § V; Ord. of 9-27-2000; Ord. of 9-14-2004, § V)  
Sec. 32-7. - Containerization and removal. 
(a)  All residences, commercial establishments, churches, and institutions located within the city shall have sufficient container capacity to accommodate their normal volume of garbage and trash collections. The type and size of containers as prescribed by the public works department shall be as follows: 
(1)  Type. The type of container shall be watertight, heavy-duty plastic, city-issued 96-gallon cart dumping containers. 
(2)  Size. The size of the container shall be 96 gallons in volume per container and 200 pounds in weight when filled. This container shall be specified by city council. 
(3)  Damaged, lost or stolen containers. The city shall not assume responsibility for any containers that are, through no fault of the city, damaged, lost or stolen. Property owners/tenants shall be jointly or severally responsible for the replacement of such containers. 
(b)  In placing carts and refuse for collection and removal, establishments, churches and institutions shall do the following: 
(1)  Household garbage. Household garbage must be placed in 96-gallon, city-issued carts for collection by the public works department at the curb or designated pickup site by 8:00 a.m. on the scheduled pickup days only. Empty carts shall be removed as soon as possible after pickup, but not later than 7:00 p.m. on the scheduled pickup days. 
(2)  If normally generating more refuse than can be contained in one 96-gallon city-issued cart per week, the establishment will be required to purchase a second city-issued cart. 
(3)  All loose materials which normally fit into carts but which are in excess as a result of special circumstances must be handled in the following manner: 
a.  Excess materials must be bagged or placed in 32-gallon trashcans with lids. 
b.  Boxes broken down, bundled and tied securely. Boxes may not be used as containers. 
c.  Large trash items shall be placed in orderly piles and tied if needed. 
(4)  Collection days as prescribed by the public works department are Monday through Friday. All solid waste categories will be collected according to a published schedule. 
(5)  Covers shall be kept on containers at all times except when depositing or removing garbage or trash. 
(6)  All refuse containers must be kept clean and sanitary. 
(7)  All apartment complexes, condominiums, and other multifamily complexes with greater than five units on a common property shall arrange for private collection. Mobile home parks with paved surface streets may be serviced by the city. In these instances, the collection vehicle shall be able to maneuver freely from limbs, brush or other obstacles and should have adequate turnaround areas to eliminate the need for reversing. Mobile home parks may also be serviced with a paved pad (concrete or asphalt or compacted ROC), which would allow the collection vehicle to back onto the pad, clearing the paved road of traffic. Carts must be placed at the rear side of the pad in accordance with subsection (b)(1) of this section. Businesses whose garbage can be accommodated by once-a-week collection in two 96-gallon or 64-gallon city-issued carts may be serviced by the city. Garbage shall be limited to household-type garbage. Wire, metals, etc., shall not be placed in carts to be collected by the city. Building materials generated by contractors shall be disposed of by the contractors. They shall be considered contractor-generated material and shall not be collected by the city. In such cases where the council deems that an unsafe condition exists (i.e, health or safety), council may deem that residential service be initiated. 
(Code 1983, § 3-2-6; Ord. of 12-10-1996, § VI; Ord. of 10-14-1997; Ord. of 9-27-2000; Ord. of 9-14-2004, § VI)  
Sec. 32-8. - Frequency of garbage collection. 
The city shall have the authority to collect garbage and waste at such times and intervals as deemed necessary for the health and sanitation of the community. 
(Code 1983, § 3-2-7; Ord. of 12-10-1996, § VII; Ord. of 9-27-2000; Ord. of 9-14-2004, § VII)  
Sec. 32-9. - Keeping property clean. 
(a)  It shall be the responsibility of the owner, agent, lessee or occupant to keep the exterior of private and public property free of litter and unsightly growth. All material generated as a result of neglect shall be the responsibility of the property owner for removal and disposal. 
(b)  It shall be the responsibility of the owner, contractor or individual performing construction or remodeling work at a construction or residential site to remove all unsightly litter at the end of each workweek. 
(Code 1983, § 3-2-8; Ord. of 12-10-1996, § VIII; Ord. of 9-27-2000; Ord. of 9-14-2004, § VIII)  
Chapter 34 - STREETS, SIDEWALKS AND OTHER PUBLIC PROPERTY[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference— Streets and sidewalks, S.C. Code 1976, § 5-7-10 et seq.; issuance of permits to charitable groups to solicit funds from motorists, S.C. Code 1976, § 5-27-910; municipality may establish a farm marketing center, S.C. Code 1976, § 46-19-110; municipal authority to regulate processions on highways, S.C. Code 1976, § 56-5-710(3). 
 
ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 
 
Sec. 34-1. - Public works department established. 
(a)  There is hereby established a public works department to be headed by a public works director who shall be appointed by and serve at the pleasure of the city council. 
(b)  The public works department shall consist of such officers and employees as shall be approved by the city council. 
(Code 1983, § 3-1-1; Ord. of 1-14-2003; Ord. No. 4-2007, § 9, 3-13-2007)  
Sec. 34-2. - Approval of names of new streets. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to lay out any new street within the city without first procuring from the council approval of the name to be assigned to the new street. 
(Code 1983, § 3-1-2)  
Sec. 34-3. - Street and roadway acceptance. 
No street or roadway shall be accepted until it has been paved or surface treated in a manner acceptable to the city. 
(Code 1983, § 3-1-3)  
Sec. 34-4. - Requirements for lots draining toward sidewalk. 
Every person owning any lot which drains toward a sidewalk shall provide suitable and proper drainage under the sidewalk as will deliver the gutter and drainage water from the lot to the drainage system of the adjoining streets. 
(Code 1983, § 3-1-4)  
Sec. 34-5. - Numbering of lots and properties. 
(a)  All property owners, residents, lessees or lessors of property are hereby required to adequately mark or number their lots, residences, establishments or places of business in an appropriate manner, attaching the numbers designated by city council, as shown on the attached plan. 
(b)  All property owners, residents, lessees and lessors of property are hereby required to number their residences, lots, establishments or places of business, using numbers of adequate size and placing them in such a position that they may be clearly and easily seen from the street in the nighttime and in the daytime. 
(c)  All property owners, residents, lessees or lessors are requested to use standard size numbers in order to make the numbering as uniform as possible. 
(d)  The clerk-treasurer and chief of police are required to revise the numbering plan from time to time as designated by the city council. 
(Code 1983, § 3-1-5)  
Sec. 34-6. - Crime watch signs. 
The city administrator is authorized to place crime watch signs on highway rights-of-way in areas which are designated as crime watch areas. Placement, replacement and site locations for the signs shall be accomplished in strict accordance with state highway department regulations. 
(Code 1983, § 3-1-6; Ord. of 5-13-1986)  
Secs. 34-7—34-30. - Reserved.  
ARTICLE II. - EXCAVATION AND OBSTRUCTION 
 
Sec. 34-31. - Excavation permit required. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to dig up, mutilate or make an excavation in any paved or unpaved street or sidewalk for any purpose without a permit from the director of public works. 
(Code 1983, § 3-1-21)  
Sec. 34-32. - Backfilling and resurfacing. 
It shall be the duty of the person making any excavation hereunder to fill the excavation and restore the surface to a condition at least equal to the surface prior to the excavation. If so required by the council, the person making an excavation shall furnish a bond, deposit or other security sufficient to ensure compliance with this section; provided, however, that the city may elect to fill and resurface the excavation and charge the cost thereof against the person making the excavation. 
(Code 1983, § 3-1-22)  
Sec. 34-33. - Danger signals required at excavations. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to allow any trench, ditch or excavation in any street, sidewalk or public place to remain open between sunset and sunrise, unless the trench, ditch or excavation has a sufficient number of lights properly displayed around it as danger signals to prevent accidents to persons or property. 
(Code 1983, § 3-1-23)  
Sec. 34-34. - Removing danger signals at excavations. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to remove or extinguish any light which may be placed as a signal at night to warn persons of danger from ditches, trenches, building materials, scaffolds, excavations, impediments or obstacles of any description whatsoever. 
(Code 1983, § 3-1-24)  
Sec. 34-35. - Obstructions prohibited. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to place any obstruction upon or cause to be obstructed in any manner any street, sidewalk or public way, or part thereof, so as to render the passage of persons, vehicles or other travel thereon difficult, inconvenient, dangerous or impossible except as otherwise provided in this article. This section shall not apply to any employee of the city, county or state while the employee is immediately and actively engaged in the maintenance, improvement or construction of any street, sidewalk or public way in the city. 
(Code 1983, § 3-1-25)  
Secs. 34-36—34-58. - Reserved.  
ARTICLE III. - UNLAWFUL ACTS 
 
Sec. 34-59. - Damaging city property. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to mutilate, deface or injure any public property within the corporate limits of the city, or any trees, buildings or other property, or to obstruct any street, alleyway, avenue, bridge, ditch or public road within the corporate limits of the city. 
(Code 1983, § 3-1-31)  
Sec. 34-60. - Throwing glass, nails, dangerous substances on streets or sidewalks. 
Any person who shall throw or place on any of the streets or sidewalks any glass in any shape or form, tin cans, nails, brick, pieces of iron, sticks or any other obstructions shall be guilty of a misdemeanor. 
(Code 1983, § 3-1-32)  
Sec. 34-61. - Vehicles leaking or scattering load prohibited. 
The owner or operator of every cart or other vehicle employed in removing or carrying any dirt, sawdust, sand, coal or materials liable to be blown by the wind, or any manure, filth or offensive matter of any kind or description, along or over any of the streets, shall have and keep the vehicle in such a tight and secure condition that the matter shall not be scattered or suffered to fall on any of the streets. 
(Code 1983, § 3-1-33)  
Sec. 34-62. - Vehicles prohibited on sidewalk. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to ride, propel or park any automobile, motorcycle or other vehicle upon any sidewalk, except as may be necessary in entering or leaving the premises or buildings. 
(Code 1983, § 3-1-34)  
Sec. 34-63. - Breaking, removing streetlights. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to break any lamp or electric light or to remove any electric lightbulb or otherwise from to tamper with the streetlights. 
(Code 1983, § 3-1-35)  
Sec. 34-64. - Breaking, destroying curbing prohibited; permit required for entrance to property. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to break, deface or destroy the curbing of any street, or to construct any entrance into property on any of the paved streets, unless the person shall have first obtained a permit in writing to do so from the public works director. 
(Code 1983, § 3-1-36)  
Sec. 34-65. - Burning matter on streets or sidewalks. 
It shall be unlawful to burn leaves or other matter on the streets or sidewalks. 
(Code 1983, § 3-1-37)  
Secs. 34-66—34-88. - Reserved.  
ARTICLE IV. - PARADES 
 
Sec. 34-89. - Definitions. 
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Parade means any march, procession, motorcade or promenade consisting of persons, animals or vehicles, floats or a combination thereof, having a common purpose, design, destination or goal, upon any street, road or public thoroughfare within the city, which parade, march, procession, motorcade or promenade does not comply with normal and usual traffic regulation and control.  
Sec. 34-90. - Permit required. 
No person shall engage in, participate in, aid, form or start any parade, unless a parade permit shall have been obtained from the city council, or the chief of police as designated by the city council, under the provisions of this article.  
Sec. 34-91. - Application. 
A person seeking the issuance of a permit under this article shall file an application in person on forms provided between the hours of 9:00 a.m. and 5:00 p.m. on Mondays through Fridays, legal holidays excepted, with the police chief or city administrator. An application for a permit shall be filed with the police chief or city administrator not less than ten days (Saturdays, Sundays and legal holidays excluded) nor more than 60 days, before the date upon which the parade is proposed to be conducted.  
Sec. 34-92. - Application contents. 
The application for a parade permit shall set forth the following information: 
(1)  The name, address, telephone number, and email address, if any, of the person seeking to conduct the parade; 
(2)  If the parade is proposed to be conducted for or behalf of an organization, the address and telephone number of the headquarters of the organization, and of the authorized director or manager with responsibility for the parade with the organization; 
(3)  The proposed date for the parade; 
(4)  The route to be traveled, the starting point and the termination point; 
(5)  The approximate number of persons who, and animals and vehicles which, will constitute the parade; the types of animals, and description of all vehicles, including a description of any sound amplification equipment or be used; 
(6)  The hours when the parade will start and terminate; 
(7)  The location by street names of any assembly areas for the parade; 
(8)  The time at which units of the parade will begin to assemble at the assembly area; 
(9)  If the parade is designed to be held by, and on behalf of or for, any person other than the applicant, the applicant shall file with the chief of police a communication in writing from this person authorizing the applicant to apply for the permit on his behalf; 
(10)  Any additional information which the chief of police shall find reasonably necessary to a fair determination regarding issuance of a permit.  
Sec. 34-93. - Issuance of permit. 
The city council shall issue a permit as provided for under this article when, from a consideration of the application and from any other information obtained by the chief of police, he finds that: 
(1)  The conduct of the parade will not substantially interrupt the safe and orderly movement of other traffic contiguous to its route; 
(2)  The conduct of the parade will not require the diversion of so many police officers to properly police the line of movement and contiguous areas as to unreasonably diminish normal police protection of the city; 
(3)  The conduct of the parade will not require the diversion of so many emergency vehicles and ambulances so as to unreasonably diminish normal service to the city; 
(4)  The concentration of persons, animals and vehicles at assembly points of the parade will not unduly interfere with proper fire and police protection of, or ambulance service to, areas contiguous to the assembly areas; 
(5)  The conduct of the parade will not unduly interfere with the movement of firefighting equipment en route to a fire; 
(6)  The parade is scheduled to move from its point of origin to its point of termination expeditiously and without unreasonable delays; 
(7)  The conduct of the parade will not interfere or conflict with any other parade for which a permit has been issued; 
(8)  No other parade permit has been granted, or is under consideration, for any portion of the time sought by the applicant, nor shall a permit be granted for a parade which will commence after sunset; 
(9)  The parade is not to be held for the sole purpose of advertising any product or goods and is not designed to be held purely for private profit.  
Sec. 34-94. - Permit contents. 
Each parade permit shall state the following information: 
(1)  The starting and conclusion times for the parade; 
(2)  What portions of the streets to be traversed may be occupied by the parade; 
(3)  The maximum length of the parade in miles and fractions thereof; 
(4)  The assembly and disbanding areas, and times for each; 
(5)  That the amplification of sound permitted to be emitted from amplification equipment be fixed and not variable; 
(6)  That the permit holder shall advise all parade participants, either orally or in writing, of the terms and conditions of the permit, prior to commencement of the parade; 
(7)  Any other information that the city administrator and chief of police shall find reasonably necessary for the protection of persons or property.  
Sec. 34-95. - Alternate permit. 
The police chief or city administrator, in denying an application for a parade permit, is empowered to authorize the conduct of a parade on a date, at a time or over a route different from that named by the applicant. An applicant desiring to accept an alternate permit shall file a written notice of acceptance with the police chief or city administrator at least ten days prior to the alternate commencement date. An alternate parade permit shall conform to the requirement of, and shall have the effect of, a parade permit under this article.  
Sec. 34-96. - Compliance by permit holder. 
A permit holder shall comply with all permit directions and conditions, all application commitments and with all applicable laws and ordinances. The parade chairperson or other person heading or leading the parade shall carry the parade permit on his person during the parade.  
Sec. 34-97. - Appeal procedure. 
Any applicant aggrieved by the denial of a parade application, or of a condition that he deems unreasonable, shall have the right to appeal to the city council. Notice of appeal shall be filed by the applicant in writing with the presiding officer of the city council within two days of the denial or notice of the condition; Saturdays, Sundays, and legal holidays are excluded. The presiding officer shall place the appeal on the agenda for the next regular meeting of the board, provided there is a meeting scheduled within ten days of the filing of the notice of appeal. If no regularly scheduled meeting is scheduled within ten days after the filing of the notice of appeal, the presiding officer shall call a special meeting to be held within ten days of the filing of the notice of appeal. The applicant may agree, in writing, to an extension of the time for holding this meeting. The city council shall consider the appeal and may reverse, affirm or modify in any regard the determination of the police chief or city administrator.  
Sec. 34-98. - Revocation of permit. 
The police chief or city administrator shall have the authority to revoke a permit issued by him, upon violation of standards for issuance of said permit as set forth, or when, by reason of disaster, emergency, public calamity, riot, or other civil or military disturbance, the safety of the public or property requires revocation. Notice of the revocation shall be delivered in writing to the permit holder in person or by certified mail.  
Sec. 34-99. - Public conduct during parades. 
(a)  No person shall unreasonably hamper, obstruct or impede, or interfere with, any parade or public assembly or with any person, vehicle or animal participating in a parade or public assembly. 
(b)  No driver of a vehicle shall drive between the vehicles or persons comprising a parade when the vehicles or persons are in motion and are conspicuously designated as a parade, unless specifically authorized to do so by a law enforcement officer. 
(c)  The chief of police shall have the authority, when reasonably necessary, to prohibit or restrict the parking of vehicles along a highway, street or road, or part thereof, constituting a part of the parade route. The chief of police shall post "no parking" signs, and it shall be unlawful for any person to park or leave unattended any vehicle in violation thereof. No person shall be liable for parking on a street where "no parking" signs are not posted pursuant to this section.  
Sec. 34-100. - Obstructing streets by assembling. 
Any person who shall assemble a crowd or hold a public meeting in any street without a parade permit, as provided in this article, shall, upon conviction, be punished as set forth in section 1-12.  
Secs. 34-101—34-121. - Reserved.  
ARTICLE V. - FILMING 
 
Sec. 34-122. - Filming regulations. 
(a)  Residential areas. A permit is required for any film, video or still photography activity (hereinafter the "filming activity), whether on public or private property, to be conducted within the city limits, with the exception that news coverage and production companies with a cast and crew totaling ten persons or less do not require such a permit. Application shall be on the city's application form to be obtained from the Building and Codes' office, and shall be submitted to the city administrator at least five business days before commencement of the filming activity. Upon the showing of exceptional circumstances which prevent the applicant's timely submission of a permit application, the city administrator shall have the discretion to allow an untimely permit application, taking into consideration the size, scale and potential impact of the proposed activity upon the area, citizens, businesses and residents to be affected. Applicants are advised that early application is encouraged in order to allow necessary time to resolve any difficulties associated with the filming activity. 
No filming activity which involves the use of explosives, pyrotechnics, fire or other special effects which involve flames or incendiary devices may be undertaken unless a permit has been obtained from the state fire marshal's office and approved in writing by the City of Hanahan Fire Chief, or his designee. At the discretion of the City of Hanahan Fire Chief, or his designee, it may be required to have fire/EMS personnel and equipment at the location at an additional cost to the production company. 
Use of public water by way of hydrant hookup shall require coordination with and specific approval by the City of Hanahan Fire Chief, or his designee, and the Charleston Water System. Payment for any such water consumed shall be coordinated with the CWS. 
Residents, their visitors, delivery personnel and/or repair and maintenance personnel shall not be denied access to neighboring homes within the area. 
Filming activities shall not begin prior to 7:00 a.m. and will end by 11:00 p.m. Requests for night scenes extending beyond the designated time window shall require prior approval granted in writing by the city administrator. 
Prior to arrival, a parking plan must be developed and approved by the city administrator and the chief of police or his designee. The plan should detail off-site parking of equipment or support vehicles not in use, as well as any large trucks or trailers used by the company. The plan should detail staging of production vehicles, and should include a statement of approval from any private property owner on whose property those vehicles may be parked. 
Lighting for filming, both during the day and night, shall be oriented away from neighboring residences wherever possible, and shall not interfere with the safe movement of traffic. 
Base camps and dressing room trailers should be parked away from neighboring residences wherever possible. 
Base camps and equipment trucks moving into or out of residential areas shall not do so before 6:00 a.m. or after 11:00 p.m. unless specifically approved in the permit, or by written authorization of the city administrator. 
If a selected zoned residential area is wanting to be used and that area has a governing homeowners association (HOA), a letter must be obtained from the HOA president or governing HOA body and submitted to the city administrator at least five days prior to the filming start date for approval. 
If at any point the filming activity is deemed a nuisance due to the disruption of the peace or poses a safety hazard to people and/or property, the chief of police and/or fire chief, or their designees, may order the immediate ceasing of all filming activity until it is deemed appropriate to resume filming activities. 
(b)  Business/industrial areas. No less than five business days prior to commencement of the filming activity, the filming company shall notify in writing all businesses and residents affected by the proposed activity. The filming company shall provide a signed copy of such notification to the city administrator. Where the planned activity may have a significant and/or prolonged impact on the normal activities of the area (for example, activities impacting parking or traffic in areas zoned as business and/or industrial), the city administrator shall have the discretion to require earlier notification. The city administrator shall be satisfied with the compliance of said notifications before the issuance of the filming permit. 
After commencement of the filming activity, the film company shall provide written notification to the affected businesses and residents of any subsequent changes to the information provided in the original notification and of any additional variances or permits granted by the city to the filming company. 
Base camps and equipment trucks moving into or out of business and/or industrial areas shall not do so before 5:00 a.m. or after 1:00 a.m. unless specifically approved in the permit, or by written authorization of the city administrator. 
Filming activities shall not begin prior to 6:00 a.m. and will end by 1:00 a.m. Requests for night scenes extending beyond the designated time window shall require prior approval granted in writing by the city administrator. 
If at any point filming activity is deemed a nuisance due to the disruption of the peace or interferes with the normal day to day operations of businesses not directly involved with the filming location or poses a safety hazard to people and/or property, the chief of police and/or fire chief, or their designees, may order the immediate ceasing of all filming activity until it is deemed appropriate to resume filming activities. 
(c)  Care of location. All properties utilized for the film activity shall be left clean and orderly and shall be restored to their previous condition, including public and private lands. The city shall be reimbursed by the permit applicant for all costs of restoring and/or repairing public property due to damage resulting from the filming activity. The city administrator may, in his sole discretion, require the filming company to pay a bond to guarantee the restoration of the location if the city administrator determines that the proposed activity may cause damage to or require extensive restoration of public property. 
(d)  Traffic control and street closures. The permit application must specify whether the film activity will disrupt the normal flow of traffic within the affected area. Traffic control, if necessary as determined by the city administrator, shall be handled through a contract with the City of Hanahan Police Department. The city administrator, in consultation with the police chief, or his designee, shall determine the number of officers needed. Intermittent holding of traffic shall not exceed three-minute intervals except when specifically approved in the permit. 
Except in exceptional circumstances, complete closure of streets shall be discouraged. Requests for temporary street closure or diverting of traffic must be approved by the South Carolina Department of Transportation where state streets or rights-of-way are involved. Berkeley County Roads and Bridges and SCDOT must also grant approval for temporary street closures or diverting of traffic if the road/street is maintained by the County of Berkeley or SCOOT. Requests for street closure or diverting of traffic must be made well enough in advance to allow for planning rerouting, or alternate routes, and for proper signage. 
(e)  Notification. The area to be covered by the notification prescribed in (a) above shall be a minimum of one block radius in each direction from the perimeter of the planned activity. Based upon the nature of the planned activity, the city administrator shall have the discretion to specify a wider area of notification as a condition of issuance of the permit. 
Notification will include all available information concerning the location and duration of the filming, prep and wrap activities, the times of day required for each location, proposed parking restrictions and restrictions on public streets, proposed location for all support facilities, as well as specifics regarding the use of lights, noise and any special effects or extraordinary equipment. The notification shall also include the film company's production office telephone number and the location manager's telephone/cell phone/pager numbers, as well as the office/pager number of the city administrator. The notification shall also inform that any concerns, objections or complaints pertaining to the planned activity may be registered the city administrator, the police department or the office of building and codes. 
(f)  Insurance. Filming companies shall be required to have liability insurance in the minimum amount of $1,000,000.00 covering bodily injury, including death and property, with the City of Hanahan and the "City of Hanahan officials and agents" named as additional insureds in said policy. A larger amount of insurance may be required by the city administrator if, in his sole discretion, he determines that the nature of the proposed film activity necessitates an increased coverage. 
(g)  Indemnity. Filming companies in the city shall agree to indemnify and hold harmless the City of Hanahan from all damages, suits, actions or liabilities, including payment of all attorney's fees, resulting from acts of the filming company or its agents during the filming activity or occurring as a result of the use of filming locations by the filming company. 
(Ord. No. 9-2015, 10-13-2015)  
Chapter 36 - TRAFFIC AND MOTOR VEHICLES[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference— Uniform Act Regulating Traffic on Highways, local authority, S.C. Code 1976, § 56-5-30; general rules regarding maximum speed limits, S.C. Code 1976, § 56-5-1520; alteration of speed limits by local authorities, signs and approval by state, S.C. Code 1976, § 56-5-1540; powers of local authorities concerning traffic laws, S.C. Code 1976, § 56-5-710. 
 
ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 
 
Secs. 36-1—36-18. - Reserved.  
ARTICLE II. - TRAFFIC REGULATIONS  
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 
 
Sec. 36-19. - Adoption of state law. 
There is hereby adopted by reference and made a part hereof as if set out in full those provisions of state law known as the Uniform Act Regulating Traffic on Highways, as contained in S.C. Code 1976, title 56, ch. 5. 
Editor's note— The cited state law may be incorporated by reference in an ordinance by municipalities. Op. Atty. Gen., No. 2460, p. 125 (1967—1968). Municipalities may further regulate traffic, provided the additional regulations do not conflict with state law, S.C. Code 1976, §§ 56-5-30 and 56-5-710. 
(Code 1983, § 8-1-1)  
Sec. 36-20. - Only licensed operators may drive vehicles. 
No vehicle shall be operated within the city limits other than by a properly licensed driver. 
(Code 1983, § 8-1-2)  
Sec. 36-21. - Obedience to traffic signals. 
Drivers of all vehicles shall abide by signals of traffic officers and all automatic and stationary traffic signs and signals within the city limits. 
(Code 1983, § 8-1-3)  
Sec. 36-22. - Authority of chief of police to make special regulations, erect signs, etc. 
The chief of police, with the approval of the council, shall have authority to make, promulgate and enforce special traffic regulations, including the designation of one-way streets, dangerous intersections where traffic shall be required to slow or stop, school zones, safety zones and regulations as to parking, nonparking and time limits for parking, and to cause to be erected or placed signs, signals, markings or other traffic control devices for the purpose of enforcing the same. These special regulations shall not become effective until they shall have been advertised two times in a daily newspaper of general circulation in the city. Any person failing or refusing to obey any regulation so advertised shall be guilty of violation of this article. 
(Code 1983, § 8-1-4) 
State Law reference— Local traffic control devices must conform with state manual of standards and specifications for uniform systems of traffic control devices, S.C. Code 1976, § 56-6-940.  
Sec. 36-23. - Impounding vehicles. 
Any unoccupied and unattended vehicle found violating the terms of this article may be removed and impounded by any police officer or duly authorized person and shall be surrendered to the duly identified owner thereof only upon payment of cost of impounding. 
(Code 1983, § 8-1-5)  
Sec. 36-24. - Hitchhiking prohibited. 
No person shall stand in any street or street right-of-way, sidewalk or curb for the purpose of soliciting a ride from a driver of any vehicle. 
(Code 1983, § 8-1-6) 
State Law reference— Similar state law, S.C. Code 1976, § 56-6-3180.  
Sec. 36-25. - Authority of police to accept cash bail in traffic offenses. 
When any person is apprehended by a city police officer upon a charge of violating any city or state traffic ordinance or law, the enforcement of which by the officer is authorized, the person so charged upon being served with the official summons issued by the arresting officer, in lieu of being immediately brought before the municipal judge, recorder or other judicial officer to enter into a formal recognizance or make direct deposit of a sum of money in lieu of a recognizance or incarceration, may deposit with the apprehending police officer a sum of money, not less than the minimum or more than the maximum fine, but in no case to exceed $100.00 to be in due course turned over to the judicial officer as money for bail in lieu of entering into a recognizance for his appearance for trial as set in the aforesaid summons or being incarcerated by the arresting officer and held for further action by the appropriate judicial officer. A receipt for the sum so deposited shall be given to the person by the arresting officer shall release the person so charged as above and provide for his further appearance before the proper judicial officer as provided for and required by the summons. 
(Code 1983, § 8-1-7; Ord. of 4-8-1974)  
Sec. 36-26. - Removal of glass from streets after removal of wrecked vehicle. 
Anyone removing a wrecked or damaged vehicle from a street or highway shall remove any glass or other injurious substance dropped from the vehicle. Any person failing or refusing to remove the injurious substance shall be guilty of a misdemeanor. 
(Code 1983, § 8-1-8; Ord. of 4-8-1974)  
Sec. 36-27. - Opening doors of vehicles. 
No person shall open the door of a vehicle unless and until this movement can be made with reasonable safety. Any person violating this section shall be guilty of a misdemeanor. 
(Code 1983, § 8-1-9; Ord. of 4-8-1974)  
Sec. 36-28. - Riding on outside of vehicle. 
It shall be unlawful for anyone to ride on the outside of a motor vehicle or anywhere except within the body thereof; provided that the provisions of this section shall not apply to persons riding motorcycles or other two-wheel vehicles. Anyone violating the provisions of this section shall be guilty of a misdemeanor. 
(Code 1983, § 8-1-10; Ord. of 4-8-1974)  
Sec. 36-29. - Boarding and alighting vehicle while in motion. 
No person shall board or alight from any vehicle while the vehicle is in motion, and no operator of any vehicle shall load or unload passengers except when the vehicle is stopped at the curb or other stopping area, and then only when this movement can be made with safety. Any person violating this section shall be guilty of a misdemeanor. 
(Code 1983, § 8-1-11; Ord. of 4-8-1974)  
Sec. 36-30. - Special regulation or prohibition of specified classes or sizes of vehicles; posting of notices. 
No truck with more than six wheels or more than two axles shall be operated on Murray Drive between Berkeley Street and Railroad Avenue except those trucks having an origin or destination on the street or which origin or destination can be reached only by using the street or parts thereof. The notice shall be posted at conspicuous places at cross roads and road junctions with the section of highway or street to which such notice shall apply. After any such notice shall have been posted, the operation of any motor vehicle or combination contrary to its provisions shall constitute a violation of this chapter. 
(Ord. No. 12-2013, 1-14-2014) 
State Law reference— Similar provisions, S.C. Code 1976, § 56-5-4210, Penalty § 56-5-6190.  
Secs. 36-31—36-46. - Reserved.  
DIVISION 2. - OPERATION OF VEHICLE[2] 

Footnotes: 
--- (2) --- 
State Law reference— General rules as to maximum speed limits, S.C. Code 1976, § 56-5-1520; alteration of speeds by local authorities, S.C. Code 1976, § 56-5-1580. 
 
Sec. 36-47. - Speed restrictions. 
(a)  No person shall drive or ride a vehicle on a street at a speed greater or less than is reasonable and prudent under the conditions then existing. 
(b)  Except as otherwise provided, no vehicle shall be operated at a speed in excess of 30 miles per hour in any urban district of the city. 
(c)  The speed limit for the streets or portions of streets within the city shall be as indicated by signs giving notice thereof that are erected upon the street or portion thereof with approval of the council. 
(Code 1983, § 8-1-21)  
Sec. 36-48. - Obedience to no-turn signs and turning markers. 
Whenever authorized signs are erected indicating that no right or left turn or U-turn is permitted, no driver of a vehicle shall disobey the directions of the sign. When authorized marks, buttons or other indicators are placed within an intersection indicating the course to be traveled by vehicles turning thereat, no driver of a vehicle shall disobey the direction of these indicators. 
(Code 1983, § 8-1-22)  
Sec. 36-49. - Zone of quiet. 
Whenever authorized signs are erected indicating a zone of quiet, and in the vicinity of hospitals, schools during school hours or churches during hours of worship, no person operating a motor vehicle shall sound the horn or other warning device of the vehicle, except in an emergency. 
(Code 1983, § 8-1-23)  
Sec. 36-50. - Stop signs at intersections. 
When stop signs are erected upon streets, every driver of a vehicle shall stop at every sign or at a clearly marked stop line before entering the intersection, except when directed to proceed by a police officer or traffic control signal. 
(Code 1983, § 8-1-24)  
Sec. 36-51. - Stop before entering a through street. 
When stop signs are erected upon streets intersecting a through street, at the entrances of a through street or at the entrance to any intersection, every driver of a vehicle shall stop at every sign or at a clearly marked stop line before entering the intersection, except when directed to proceed by a police officer or traffic control signal. 
(Code 1983, § 8-1-25)  
Sec. 36-52. - Driving across private property; U-turns prohibited. 
(a)  It shall be unlawful for any person driving a vehicle to use the driveway of any filling station or service station as a roadway or thoroughfare. 
(b)  It shall be unlawful for any person driving a vehicle to make any U-turn or other turn prohibited at any point where the turn is prohibited, and it shall be unlawful to accomplish a U-turn by deviously going into or through private property adjoining the street where the turn is prohibited. 
(Code 1983, § 8-1-26)  
Sec. 36-53. - One-way streets. 
Upon those streets and parts of streets where the direction for traffic is designated by signs, vehicular traffic shall move only in the indicated direction when signs indicating the direction of traffic are erected and maintained. 
(Code 1983, § 8-1-27)  
Sec. 36-54. - Regulations for parades or processions. 
No parade or procession, except the forces of the United States Army or Navy, the military forces of the state and the forces of the police and fire department, shall occupy, march or proceed along any street except in accordance with a permit issued by the clerk-treasurer's office and approved by the chief of police and any other regulations as are set forth in this article which may apply. 
(Code 1983, § 8-1-28)  
Sec. 36-55. - Vehicles not to be driven on sidewalk. 
The driver of a vehicle shall not drive a vehicle within a sidewalk area except at a permanent or temporary driveway, and then shall not block the driveway or sidewalk provided for the use of pedestrians. 
(Code 1983, § 8-1-29)  
Sec. 36-56. - Careless operation of a motor vehicle. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to operate any vehicle without care and caution and full regard for the safety of persons and property. Any person failing to do so shall be guilty of careless driving or riding. The operation of any vehicle when the same or any of its appliances is not in proper or safe condition shall be prima facie evidence of careless driving or riding. Careless operation may be a lesser included offense of reckless driving. 
(Code 1983, § 8-1-30; Ord. of 6-14-1983)  
Secs. 36-57—36-85. - Reserved.  
ARTICLE III. - STOPPING, STANDING AND PARKING[3] 

Footnotes: 
--- (3) --- 
State Law reference— Local authority to regulate standing or parking of vehicles, S.C. Code 1976, § 56-5-710(1); municipalities with marked parking spaces must designate spaces for disabled persons, S.C. Code 1976, § 56-3-1965. 
 
Sec. 36-86. - Parking prohibited on certain streets. 
No person shall park a vehicle where signs prohibiting parking are erected on streets. 
(Code 1983, § 8-2-1)  
Sec. 36-87. - No stopping or parking near hazardous or congested places. 
When signs are erected upon approach to hazardous or congested places, no person shall stop, stand or park a vehicle in any designated place. 
(Code 1983, § 8-2-2)  
Sec. 36-88. - Parking as to obstruct street prohibited. 
No person shall stop, stand or park any vehicle upon a street in such a manner as to leave available less than ten feet of the width of the roadway for the free movement of vehicular traffic; except that a driver shall stop when necessary in obedience to traffic regulations, traffic signs, signals or a police officer. 
(Code 1983, § 8-2-3)  
Sec. 36-89. - Parking prohibited during certain hours in designated places. 
When signs are erected in a block giving notice thereof, no person shall park a vehicle between the hours and on the days so designated. 
(Code 1983, § 8-2-4)  
Sec. 36-90. - Parking time limited in designated places. 
When signs are erected in a block giving notice thereof, no person shall park a vehicle for longer than the period and between the hours so designated. 
(Code 1983, § 8-2-5)  
Sec. 36-91. - Parking for loading only. 
(a)  No person shall stop, stand or park a vehicle for any purpose or period of time other than for the expeditious loading or unloading of passengers in any place designated as a passenger zone. 
(b)  No person shall stop, stand or park a vehicle for any purpose or length of time other than for the expeditious unloading and delivery or pickup and loading of material in any place designated as a loading zone during hours when the provisions applicable to loading zones are in effect. 
(Code 1983, § 8-2-6)  
Sec. 36-92. - Bus stops and taxicab stands. 
(a)  The driver of a bus or taxicab shall not stand or park upon any street at any place other than at a bus stop or taxicab stand, respectively; except that this provision shall not prevent the driver of any vehicle from temporarily stopping in accordance with other stopping or parking regulations for the purpose of and while actually engaged in loading or unloading passengers. 
(b)  No person shall stop, stand or park a vehicle other than a bus in a bus stop, or other than a taxicab in a taxicab stand when any stop or stand has been officially designated and appropriately signed; except that the driver of a passenger vehicle may temporarily stop therein for the purpose of and while actually engaged in loading or unloading passengers when this stopping does not interfere with any bus or taxicab waiting to enter or about to enter the zone. 
(Code 1983, § 8-2-7)  
Sec. 36-93. - Standing or parking close to curb. 
No person shall stand or park a vehicle in a roadway other than parallel with the edge of the roadway, and with the curbside wheels of the vehicle within one foot of the edge of the roadway; except that upon those streets which have been marked or signed for angle parking, vehicles shall be parked at an angle to the curb indicated by the mark or signs. Vehicles shall park on the right side of the street, except where regulations restrict parking to one side only. Whenever lines have been painted to indicate the parking area, vehicles shall be parked entirely within those lines. 
(Code 1983, § 8-2-8)  
Sec. 36-94. - Parking for certain purposes prohibited. 
No person shall stand or park a vehicle upon any roadway for the purpose of: 
(1)  Displaying it for sale; 
(2)  Advertising of any nature whatsoever; or 
(3)  Washing, greasing, storing or repairing any vehicle, except repairs necessitated by an emergency. 
(Code 1983, § 8-2-9)  
Sec. 36-95. - Parking on Swale/SCDOT right-of-way—Residential areas. 
(a)  No person shall drive, operate or park a motor vehicle in the swale area or upon any unpaved right-of-way adjacent to a paved street, avenue, or roadway, whether public or private, within the city which swale area or unpaved right-of-way abuts the property of another, without the permission of the owner, lessee or occupant of the property abutting the swale area or unpaved right-of-way. 
(b)  Nothing contained in this section shall prohibit the operation of a city vehicle, emergency vehicle on an emergency service call, or vehicle owned by a utility which is in the course of official business, to park upon the swale area anywhere within the city. 
(c)  Nothing contained herein shall prohibit any individual from driving or parking upon the swale area abutting the property owned, leased, or occupied by that individual within the city limits. 
(d)  This section shall not be applicable if it is otherwise allowed within a planned unit development or condominium association that by its rules, regulations, or bylaws permit such vehicles. 
(Ord. No. 1-2013, 2-12-2013)  
Secs. 36-96—36-116. - Reserved.  
ARTICLE IV. - WRECKERS  
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 
 
Sec. 36-117. - Definitions. 
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Class means a wrecker capability based upon size and weight handling characteristics. The term "class" is synonymous with the term "category" and shall be used interchangeably. 
Fee means a monetary amount charged for a service provided. The term "fee" is synonymous with the terms "rate" and "charge" and shall be used interchangeably. 
Night service means wrecker service operations which commence in the hours between 6:00 p.m. and 6:00 a.m. Commencement of operations shall be considered as the time a call for service is requested. 
(Ord. of 4-12-2005, art. A; Ord. of 6-14-2005, § 3)  
Sec. 36-118. - Financial interest of police officers or city employees. 
No city police officer or other city employee shall hold any financial interest or any form of ownership interest in any wrecker service utilized by the city. 
(Ord. of 4-12-2005, art. B, § 8-3-1)  
Sec. 36-119. - Choice of service. 
Unless the owner or driver of a vehicle is incapacitated or unavailable, the owner or driver of a wrecked or disabled vehicle shall have the wrecker service of his choice called. 
(Ord. of 4-12-2005, art. B, § 8-3-2)  
Sec. 36-120. - Recommending services. 
No city police officer or other city employee will recommend any wrecker service to the owner or driver of a wrecked or disabled vehicle during the performance of their duties. 
(Ord. of 4-12-2005, art. B, § 8-3-3)  
Sec. 36-121. - Complaints. 
(a)  Complaints from or about wrecker services regarding an incident involving the police department or its operation of the wrecker rotation list must be received, in writing, within 15 business days of the alleged incident. All written complaints shall be directed to the chief of police. 
(b)  The complaint will be reviewed regarding its validity and the chief of police or a designee will determine a reasonable and fair solution to the complaint. 
(Ord. of 4-12-2005, art. G, § 8-3-27)  
Sec. 36-122. - Suspension or removal procedures; penalties. 
(a)  A wrecker service may be suspended or removed from the list in the following manner: 
(1)  The violation of any traffic laws while responding to or returning from a call may result in the immediate removal of that wrecker service from the wrecker rotation list. 
(2)  Any actions by any wrecker driver that adversely affects the reputation of the police department may result in the immediate removal of that wrecker service from the wrecker rotation list. 
(3)  If the police department has reason to believe that a wrecker service has failed to remain in compliance with the qualification criteria set out in division 2 of this article, that the noncompliance continues, and that the noncompliance will be detrimental to the public may result in the immediate removal of that wrecker service from the wrecker rotation list. 
(4)  The failure of any wrecker service to notify the police department of its unavailability, in a timely manner, may result in its suspension from the wrecker rotation list for a period of up to 90 days. Three suspensions from the rotation list in a two-year period shall result in a permanent removal from the list. 
(b)  Penalties for violations of this article that do not directly affect the safety of the public shall be as follows: 
(1)  First offense: warning letter. 
(2)  Second offense: 90-day suspension from rotation. 
(3)  Subsequent offense: removal from the list. 
(Ord. of 4-12-2005, art. G, § 8-3-28)  
Secs. 36-123—36-138. - Reserved.  
DIVISION 2. - QUALIFICATION CRITERIA 
 
Sec. 36-139. - Licensing. 
The wrecker service must hold a valid business license from the city. 
(Ord. of 4-12-2005, art. C, § 8-3-4)  
Sec. 36-140. - Responsiveness and availability. 
(a)  The wrecker service must be able to safely respond from the time of notification to any given location within the city within 20 minutes between the hours of 6:00 a.m. and 6:00 p.m. and 30 minutes between 6:00 p.m. and 6:00 a.m. 
(b)  The wrecker service offices and storage location must be within a reasonable distance from the corporate limits of the city in order to be able to respond within the time specified in subsection (a) of this section and to be convenient for the owner or driver of the wrecked or disabled vehicle. The chief of police or a designee will make the determination of a reasonable distance. 
(Ord. of 4-12-2005, art. C, § 8-3-5; Ord. of 6-14-2005, § 1)  
Sec. 36-141. - Storage area and fee. 
The wrecker service shall maintain a safe storage area for all vehicles towed. This may be a locked building or a secured, fenced-in area where the stored vehicle and other property shall not be accessible to the public. A wrecker service may charge a fee for storage. Such fees shall not commence prior to 24 hours after the tow is completed, and only if the vehicle is actually placed in storage. Fees shall be determined in accordance with division 5 of this article. 
(Ord. of 4-12-2005, art. C, § 8-3-6)  
Sec. 36-142. - Basic equipment and identification. 
(a)  All wreckers shall have appropriate safety equipment, fire extinguishers, warning devices, flashlights and all other equipment necessary to protect the motoring public and shall be equipped with amber flashing lights visible in all directions for a distance of 500 feet in normal sunlight. Such equipment shall be maintained in good working order. All authorized amber flashing lights shall be activated and wrecker operators shall wear reflective traffic safety vests while performing recovery operations or when circumstances are such that the vehicles being transported create a potentially hazardous condition for other motorists. 
(b)  Each wrecker service on the rotation list must place a sign on the driver and front passenger door of each of its wreckers indicating the company name, address, and telephone number of the zone to which it is assigned. This sign shall be painted on the doors of the wrecker or otherwise permanently affixed to the doors. The letters of the sign must be no less than two inches high. If the wrecker is registered in a name other than that of the wrecker service, the owner's name must also appear on the doors in letters no less than one inch high. All lettering on wreckers shall be plainly visible and shall be in a color in contrast to that of the wrecker. 
(c)  Each wrecker service on the rotation list must place a sign on the exterior of its business location clearly visible indicating the company name, telephone number, and business hours. 
(Ord. of 4-12-2005, art. C, § 8-3-7)  
Sec. 36-143. - Insurance. 
(a)  Each wrecker service on the rotation list shall carry liability insurance on its wreckers and its premises in an amount not less than $300,000.00 for a class A wrecker, $500,000.00 for a class B wrecker and $750,000.00 for a class C wrecker. 
(b)  Each wrecker service on the rotation list shall carry insurance that covers vehicles, cargo, and other property in or on the vehicle during transit in an amount of not less than $75,000.00 for a class A wrecker, $150,000.00 for a class B wrecker and $250,000.00 for a class C wrecker. 
(c)  Each wrecker service on the rotation list shall carry garage keeper's liability insurance covering customer's vehicles in an amount not less than $100,000.00 for a class A wrecker, $200,000.00 for a class B wrecker and $200,000.00 for a class C wrecker. 
(d)  Each wrecker service on the rotation call list shall show proof that worker's compensation insurance is provided for its employees in accordance with S.C. Code 1976, title 42, Worker's Compensation. 
(Ord. of 4-12-2005, art. C, § 8-3-8; Ord. of 6-14-2005, § 2)  
Sec. 36-144. - Towing log. 
(a)  Each wrecker owned by any wrecker service on a rotation list shall be equipped with a towing log. The towing log shall be maintained by the wrecker service and shall accurately reflect all towing done by the wrecker service at the request of the police department.
