Notes:   1) Stormwater drainage standards are specified in Section 5.11, below. 
2) Sidewalk standards are specified in Section 5.7, below. 

(A)	An alley shall be no longer than three hundred (300) feet without intersecting a local or collector road. Alleys shall not intersect arterial roads or highways. 
(B)	Internal circulation roads provide off-site access to residential, commercial, office, and similar units in larger land developments, such as apartment complexes, shopping centers and malls, and office parks. Internal circulation roads link external roads to parking aisles or private garages. 
(C)	Collector roads shall be designed as through roads, where practical, to utilize their capacity and to reduce strain on intersecting collector and arterial roads and highways. Techniques to calm traffic and deter heavy trucks shall be utilized in residential areas. 
(D)	Lane widths shall be the narrowest width feasible to serve the land development to calm traffic and reduce pedestrian crossing times. The table provides wider lane widths for certain roads with medians, two-way left-turn lanes, or outside lanes to be shared with bicycle traffic. 
(E)	A landscaped median may be proposed in place of a two-way left-turn lane. 
(F)	"Typical" curb radius standards are intended for roads designed for bicycle and pedestrian access and safety as well as slower vehicle speeds. The planning commission may allow larger radii for existing roads with higher design speeds and/or an unusually high percentage of heavy truck traffic. 
5.6.7.   Bike lanes.
    Dedicated bike lanes four (4) to six (6) feet wide shall be provided on all proposed roads designed with a target speed greater than thirty (30) miles per hour. Bike lanes may coincide with emergency lanes, where applicable. 
5.6.8.   On-street parking.

(A)	Parking provided adjacent to the road, whether or not within a road right-of-way, shall be designed to allow safe and efficient movement into and out of travel lanes. Parking stalls shall be spatially separated from through-lanes to provide visibility for motorists driving, parking, or disembarking parked vehicles. This separation shall typically range from two (2) to ten (10) feet, depending on the target speed and traffic volume of the road. No such separation shall be required for parking aisles. 
(B)	No parking shall be designed to allow more than twenty (20) feet between the parking stall and the through-lane where motorists would back into the through-lane. Driveways to garages for single-family attached and detached homes shall be exempt. 
(C)	Parallel parking. On-street parallel parking spaces should be twenty (20) to twenty-two (22) feet in length and seven (7) to nine (9) feet in width from face of curb. 
(D)	Angled and perpendicular parking. Design standards for on-street angled and perpendicular parking shall be identical to those for on-site parking, Section 5.9.3, below. 
5.6.9.   Tree planting along roadways.

(A)	Street trees. The developer shall install street trees along arterial, commercial collector, and internal circulation roads in a major land development to calm traffic, buffer private property from light and noise of traffic, shade the road and sidewalks, and reduce urban heat island effect. If a road is maintained or is proposed to be maintained by a government entity that prohibits street trees, roadside trees shall be required. 
(1)	One (1) street tree shall be installed per forty (40) feet of road, on average, measured at edge of pavement, on each side of the road, exclusive of intersections with other roads. On-center spacing between street trees shall be thirty (30) to fifty (50) feet. 
(2)	If curb bulb-outs are proposed to define on-street parking, one (1) street tree may be planted in the bulb-out in place of two (2) street trees otherwise required per Subsection (A)(1), above. 
(3)	Street trees shall be upright growing hardwood trees with an average life expectancy of at least forty (40) years. 
(4)	Street trees shall be installed at three (3) inches in caliper in tree wells or in a verge (between the road and the sidewalk). 
(5)	Street trees shall be planted within the road right-of-way or easement and protected from vehicular traffic by curbs, swales, or pre-existing ditches. 
(a)	Street trees shall be planted at least two (2) feet from barrier (standing) curbs. 
(b)	Street trees shall be planted at least five (5) feet from rolled curbs. 
(6)	Conservation of an existing tree three (3) inches or more in caliper in the road right-of-way or easement may meet the requirement for a street tree. 
(B)	Roadside trees. The developer shall install roadside trees along local, residential collector, and industrial collector roads as well as highways in a major land development to calm traffic, buffer private property from light and noise of traffic, shade the road and sidewalks, and reduce urban heat island effect. 
(1)	One (1) roadside tree shall be planted per fifty (50) feet of road right-of-way, on average, measured at the edge of right-of-way, on each side of the road. On-center spacing between roadside trees shall be between twenty-five (25) and one hundred (100) feet. 
(2)	Roadside trees may be planted in the road right-of-way or easement or in the required front yard of adjoining lots. 
(3)	Roadside trees shall be upright growing hardwood trees, at least three (3) inches in caliper, with an average life expectancy of at least forty (40) years. 
(4)	At least every third roadside tree shall be a canopy tree, maturing to at least forty (40) feet in height. The remainder may be understorey trees. 
(5)	An existing tree protected by Hanahan zoning standards, within twenty-five (25) feet of the road right-of-way, shall meet the requirement for one (1) roadside tree. 
5.6.10.   Road names.
(A)	The developer shall submit road names for planning commission approval, typically within final plat review. The developer shall verify acceptability of the road names with Berkeley County E911 prior to submitting them for Hanahan Planning Commission review and approval. 
(B)	To prevent any confusion for emergency response vehicles, names for proposed roads shall be sufficiently audibly different from all other roads in the following postal zip codes, which cover Hanahan, as well as any future zip code area subdivided therefrom: 29406, 29408, and 29445. 
(C)	Road labels, such as place, street, drive, avenue, and boulevard, shall be applied to accurately represent the road. (e.g., a two-lane local road shall not be labeled a "boulevard" and a four-lane divided facility shall not be labeled a "place.") 
(D)	A road proposed to intersect a crossroad immediately opposite an existing road shall carry the same name. 
(E)	A proposed road crossing a more significant road (e.g., a local road crossing a collector) shall be labeled "East" and "West" or "North" and "South" according to the general compass orientation of the proposed road. 
5.7. - Design and improvements standards for pedestrian facilities. 
5.7.1.   General standards.
(A)	Proposed walkways shall provide at least six (6) feet lateral clearance from finished grade to seven (7) feet above finished grade. The clear distance shall be at least one (1) foot wider than the width of the walkway and shall not extend into travel lanes of adjacent roadways. 
(B)	Proposed walkways shall be at least four (4) feet wide. 
(C)	Proposed walkways shall be significantly differentiated from their surroundings by color, texture, materials, grade elevation, or any combination thereof, unless specifically stated otherwise, to prevent ponding in the walkway and to protect users from automobile traffic. 
(D)	Proposed walkways shall be constructed so as to prevent the erosion or deterioration of edges, to withstand wear and tear from expected users and adverse natural conditions and events, and to otherwise ensure their durability and longevity. 
5.7.2.   Sidewalks.
(A)	On roads with target speeds thirty (30) miles per hour or greater, sidewalks shall be separated from through-lanes on roads by at least five (5) feet, except as needed to access crosswalks. The interstitial space may be hardscaped or provided with vegetative ground cover. 
(B)	On roads with target speeds forty (40) miles per hour or greater, sidewalks shall be separated from through-lanes on roads by at least ten (10) feet, except as needed to access crosswalks. The interstitial space may be hardscaped or provided with vegetative ground cover. 
(C)	On single-loaded local roads, sidewalks shall only be required on the side of the street with proposed home sites, but shall be at least six (6) feet wide. 
(D)	On permanent single-terminus local roads, sidewalks shall only be required on one side of the street, but shall be at least six (6) feet wide. 
(E)	Proposed sidewalks shall meet or exceed standards of the Americans with Disabilities Act, as amended, including curb ramps and passing areas, as applicable. 
(F)	Sidewalks shall be constructed of concrete, bricks, granite pavers or similar hardscape on a compacted base sufficient to support the surface and reasonably expected pedestrian traffic and outdoor furniture under all weather conditions. 
(G)	Proposed sidewalks shall be constructed to withstand automobile traffic entering driveways or parking alongside the road where they are not reasonably protected from such. 
5.7.3.   Bike/ped facilities.
(A)	Facilities designed for bicycle and/or pedestrian circulation independent of a road (i.e., not a sidewalk) may be constructed with asphalt or permeable or natural surfaces like gravel. Such facilities shall be designed to ensure minimal loss of loose material over time (e.g., edging) and constructed on ground or base that adequately supports the surface material in all weather conditions while meeting the demands of expected traffic. 
(B)	Internal blocks longer than eight hundred (800) feet shall be approximately bisected by mid-block walkways to ensure adequate pedestrian access throughout the neighborhoods, except where such walkways would end in wetlands or other inaccessible features. 
(C)	Multi-use facilities proposed for bicycle and pedestrian traffic shall be at least eight (8) feet wide. Proposed two-way multi-use facilities should be at least ten (10) feet wide, which the planning commission shall require for safety and access at any point the walkway enters a road right-of-way or easement. The width of the multi-use walkway may taper thereafter, although this is discouraged. 
5.7.4.   Crosswalks.
(A)	Crosswalks shall connect all opposing curb ramps at intersections of proposed residential and commercial collector roads, arterial roads, commercial internal circulation roads, and highways. All crosswalks shall be provided with signs indicating the presence of the crosswalk in accordance with minimum SCDOT standards. 
(B)	Crosswalks on residential collector roads and commercial internal circulation roads shall be comprised, at a minimum, of two four-inch white lines meeting SCDOT raised pavement marking standards. The lateral distance between the lines shall be the same as the width of the sidewalks connected. 
(C)	Other required crosswalks shall be articulated more significantly, as acceptable to the planning commission, and shall be linked with a pedestrian crossing signal at a traffic light or with flashing yellow lights that precede the crosswalk in both directions of vehicular traffic in accordance with SCDOT standards. 
5.7.5.   Courtyards.
    A proposed courtyard shall be a park space on which proposed residential lots front and are oriented toward. Wet and dry ponds (stormwater detention and retention facilities) may be incorporated into the court as design elements. 
(A)	The courtyard shall include walkways that meet or exceed standards for local roads. 
(B)	The courtyard shall include street trees that meet or exceed standards for commercial collector roads. 
(C)	The courtyard shall be at least twenty-five (25) feet wide. 
(D)	The courtyard shall abut and be open to local roads with on-street parking on at least fifteen (15) percent of its perimeter, measured at edge of pavement and the footprints of abutting homes. 
(E)	Vehicular access shall be provided to the rear of homes located on courtyards via two-way alleys or local roads that are hardscaped and designed and engineered to accommodate service vehicles (fire truck, garbage truck, school bus, etc.). 
5.7.6   Plazas.

    A proposed plaza shall be a park space on which proposed commercial storefronts or office units front and are oriented toward. The plaza shall typically include street furniture and articulated public spaces, including but not limited to some combination of benches, water features, gazebos, stages, planter boxes, and galleries. 
(A)	The plaza shall include walkways and street trees that meet or exceed standards for commercial collector roads. 
(B)	The plaza shall be at least forty (40) feet wide and no larger than one-half (1/2) acre in size, measured to heated walls of storefronts and curbs of adjoining streets. 
(C)	Vehicular access shall be provided to the rear of stores and offices located on plazas via two-way alleys or local roads that are hardscaped and designed to accommodate service vehicles (fire truck, garbage truck, school bus, etc.). 
(D)	Plazas shall be designed to prevent regular vehicle traffic but shall accommodate aerial fire trucks so that potential fires can be fought by firefighters. 
(E)	The plaza shall abut and be open to commercial collector roads with on-street parking on at least fifteen (15) percent of its perimeter, measured from edge of pavement and the footprints of abutting homes. Break-away bollards are recommended at the opening to deter motorists but to allow access by emergency response vehicles. 
5.8. - Sanitation service. 
(A)	Curbside pick-up. Land developments proposed for curbside trash pick-up shall be designed so as to minimize backtracking by sanitation vehicles by limiting single-terminus streets and providing two (2) routes of egress from each lot to the exterior of the land development, as practical. 

(B)	Community pick-up. Land developments proposed for community trash pick-up shall locate the dumpster(s) at convenient point(s) of access for users and sanitation vehicles. To the extent practical, dumpsters shall be located along alleys or internal circulation roads that can be easily accessed by sanitation vehicles but that are not easily visible from public view. Where practical, dumpsters shall be located to the rear, and not near the public face, of structures. Screening and buffering per landscaping standards, Section 6.5 of the Hanahan Zoning Ordinance, shall apply. 
5.9. - Parking. 
5.9.1.   General standards.
(A)	All proposed parking areas shall be designed as part of a unified circulation plan that safely and efficiently provides access to each lot, land use, residence, office, shop, or similar unit. Exclusive of natural constraints, parking areas for separate parcels and land uses in a proposed land development shall be accessible to one (1) another so as to allow motorists to pass from one (1) parking area into another without reentering collector or arterial roads or highways. 
(B)	All proposed parking areas shall be designed so that sanitation, emergency, and other public service vehicles can safely and efficiently serve the development for which parking is proposed. 
(C)	Circulation areas shall be designed so that vehicles can proceed safely without posing a danger to pedestrians or parked vehicles. 
(D)	Parking areas shall be constructed of durable all-weather surfaces resistant to ponding, adequate to accommodate regular use by vehicles routinely generated by the proposed development. 
(E)	Access points. 
(1)	A parcel with less than two hundred (200) feet of road frontage shall provide no more than one (1) access point onto the road(s). For the purpose of this provision, an ingress point and a separate egress point shall be considered one (1) access point. 
(2)	A parcel with two hundred (200) feet or more of frontage shall provide no more than two (2) access points onto the road(s). For the purpose of this provision, an ingress point and a separate egress point shall be considered one (1) access point. 
(3)	Multiple parcels in a proposed land development shall be provided with shared access points, where practical, to minimize encroachments into roads, on-street parking, sidewalks, and any required buffers. 

(F)	Parking area landscaping and canopy. Planting requirements for parking areas shall be those found in Section 6.5 of the Hanahan Zoning Ordinance. 
(G)	Loading zones. The developer of a non-residential land development shall make a parking space available to the development as needed by the proposed land use. 
(1)	Each space shall be at least forty (40) feet long and within two hundred (200) feet of the structure served. 
(2)	Loading zones may occur in on-street parking or off-street parking areas and shall be designed so as not to obstruct through-lanes of local, collector, and arterial roads, highways, and one-lane alleys. 
(3)	A loading zone in a parallel parking lane on a community or public road shall be posted with signage indicating a thirty-minute parking time limit. 
(H)	Stacking stalls for drive-through service . Land uses proposed with drive-through service, such as a bank, restaurant, pharmacy, school, or car wash, shall provide stacking stalls to accommodate vehicles awaiting in-car service. The drive-through service shall not be designed in such a way that vehicles will await service in the adjoining road. 
(1)	Stacking stalls shall be at least eight (8) feet wide and twenty (20) feet long. 
(2)	The point of service (e.g., service window) is not a stacking stall. 
(3)	Restaurants shall provide eight (8) stacking stalls. 
(4)	Other land uses with one (1) point of service shall provide two (2) stacking stalls. 
(5)	Other land uses with more than one (1) point of service shall provide one (1) stacking stall per point of service. 
(I)	Off-site parking. The developer who utilizes off-site parking to satisfy parking allocation requirements shall demonstrate to the City Planner, prior to final plat approval, and the Zoning Administrator, prior to receipt of a zoning permit, that off-site parking is available to the land use proposed. This shall be demonstrated by written, attested agreement or a legal easement on the property on which the parking occurs, or the parking area may be a community parking lot, owned and operated by the City of Hanahan or a private community association in accordance with one (1) of the maintenance vehicles provided in this ordinance. 
(J)	Parking as a land use. A parking lot may be the primary use of land on a parcel, per the Hanahan Zoning Ordinance. As long as nearby land uses rely on the off-site parking area per written, attested agreement or easement approved by the City of Hanahan, necessary parking stalls shall not be eliminated. The City of Hanahan shall not be held liable for a regulatory taking for requiring the parcel to remain in use for parking. 
5.9.2.   Parking allocation requirements.
    Each lot, land use, residence, office, shop, or similar unit shall be provided parking according to the schedule below. Parking stalls to satisfy these requirements shall be provided on site, on street, off site, or some combination thereof, as specified in the schedule. 
(A)	Individual zoning districts, including approved Planned Development Districts, may modify parking allocation requirements in this chapter to meet the needs of that zoning district. 
(B)	Off-site parking shall occur within four hundred (400) feet of the structure for which the parking is required. 
(C)	On-street parking shall occur within six hundred (600) feet of the structure for which the parking is required. 
(D)	Commercial and agency vehicles - trucks and company cars - shall be allotted parking stalls in addition to the required number specified in the allocation schedule. 
(E)	High-school administrators may choose to provide parking for high school students. Administrators shall implement a program to limit parking passes so as not to exceed capacity of parking provided. Documentation of such program shall be submitted to the zoning administrator for zoning permit review and approval. 
(F)	A portion of the required stalls shall be accessible to the handicapped to comply with the federal Americans with Disabilities Act. For the purposes of this ordinance, one (1) accessible stall shall be required for each land development. In addition, one (1) of every fifty (50) stalls provided shall be accessible. The developer is encouraged to consult standards promulgated by the Act for full compliance. 
(G)	For a land use not specified in the allocation schedule and for which no similar land use is listed, the minimum required number of parking stalls shall be eighty (80) percent of the maximum number of parked vehicles generated by the land use, as found in "Parking Generation," as amended, published by the Institute of Transportation Engineers. Alternatively, the developer may generate a study for parking demand specific to the site, the results of which the planning commission may approve as the required number of stalls for the land development.

Instructive example: Five thousand (5,000) SF of retail space shares a parking lot with ten thousand (10,000) SF of office space. Thirty (30) stalls are required for the office space. Twenty (20) stalls would be required for the retail space. The latter can be discounted twenty (20) percent, resulting in sixteen (16) required stalls for the retail space, plus thirty (30) stalls for the office space, equals a forty-six-stall parking area. 
5.9.3.   Parking dimensions.
(A)	Off-street parking shall meet the minimum dimensional standards specified in the following chart, except as elsewhere specified.

(B)	Aisle width shall be at least fifteen (15) feet if parking stalls occur on only one (1) side of aisle. 
(C)	Minimum aisle width specified in the table above may be reduced by one (1) foot per three (3) inches of increased curb length. Maximum aisle reduction shall be two (2) feet. In no event shall a two-way aisle be narrower than twenty (20) feet. 
(D)	The planning commission shall uphold good engineering practices and ensure that wider spaces or aisles are incorporated in or near areas of conflict, such as entrances and curves. 
5.9.4. - Driveways. 
(A)	General standards. 
(1)	This section of the ordinance sets design standards for the facility providing access to private property; therefore the term "driveway" shall apply to an internal circulation road as well as a private single-family residential access for the purposes of this section. 
(2)	All land development proposals shall provide vehicular access to the parcel, which shall be accomplished via private access or community access and parking area. 
(3)	Driveways shall be designed with the minimum width necessary to provide safe and efficient vehicle access to the site so as to limit encroachment into pedestrian facilities, bike lanes, and on-street parking, where applicable. 
(4)	Where applicable, the developer shall obtain an encroachment permit from the entity maintaining the road. Successful receipt of an encroachment permit does not constitute approval by the City of Hanahan, which may require standards that differ from the entity issuing the encroachment permit. 
(5)	Stricter driveway standards may be imposed by zoning district. 
(B)	Standards for residential lot with on-site parking for single unit (including house, manufactured housing unit, and some townhouses). 
(1)	The driveway shall be at least eight (8) feet wide and twelve (12) feet wide at the edge of the road or alley serving the lot. 
(2)	The driveway shall be at least sixty (60) feet from the nearest intersection, measured between centerlines and shall be at least twenty (20) feet from the nearest tangent point of an intersection curb or pavement edge. 
(C)	Standards for off-street parking area with fewer than seven (7) stalls. 
(1)	A one-way driveway shall be at least twelve (12) feet wide, a two-way driveway twenty (20) feet wide. 
(2)	The driveway shall be equipped with turning radii, measured at edge of pavement, of at least ten (10) feet. 
(3)	The driveway shall be at least sixty (60) feet from the nearest intersection, measured between centerlines and shall be at least twenty (20) feet from the nearest tangent point of an intersection curb or pavement edge. 
(D)	Standards for off-street parking area with seven (7) stalls or more. 
(1)	A one-way driveway shall be at least twelve (12) feet wide, a two-way driveway twenty (20) feet wide. 
(2)	The driveway shall be equipped with turning radii, measured at edge of pavement, of at least fifteen (15) feet. 
(3)	The driveway shall be at least seventy-five (75) feet from the nearest intersection, measured between centerlines and shall be at least thirty-five (35) feet from the nearest tangent point of an intersection curb or pavement edge. 
5.10. - Illumination of vehicular and pedestrian facilities. 
(A)	The developer shall propose a system of illumination of all roads and adjacent sidewalks within a major land development. Illumination shall provide lighting for the safety of the traveling public without causing nuisances to adjoining land uses due to glare or intensity. The proposal shall meet or exceed the American National Standard Practice for Roadway Lighting, Illuminating Engineering Society of North America, 2000, as amended. 
(B)	Illumination of vehicular and pedestrian facilities in all proposed land developments shall be provided by fixtures appropriate to the facility and surrounding land uses in size, height, scale, and on-center spacing. 
5.11. - Stormwater and floodplain management. 
5.11.1.   General standards for erosion and sediment reduction and stormwater management.
(A)	The developer shall propose a stormwater management system that prevents damage to structures and land within the proposed land development, that prevents increases in stormwater run-off onto property downstream of the proposed development, and that prevents additional stormwater accumulation upstream of the proposed development. Moreover, the developer shall propose a stormwater management plan that minimizes water pollution discharges from the proposed land development to the extent practical. 
(B)	The land development shall be designed, to the extent practical, to minimize grading, filling, and alteration of land that disrupts natural drainage patterns. 
(C)	To the extent practical, structures shall not be located such that natural or artificial drainage patterns and facilities would be impeded in a manner detrimental to surrounding properties within or adjacent to the proposed land development. In addition, property boundaries shall not be platted such that future structures would impede drainage in the same manner. 
(D)	The proposed land development shall tie into the existing stormwater drainage system, where available, and shall ensure that the volume and pollution level of water drained do not adversely impact the drainage system or the receiving water body to which the system discharges. 
(E)	Primary drainage may be handled in the road system or to the interior of blocks. Bioretention swales are preferred conduits for run-off where drainage is handled to the interior of blocks. Drainage ditches are discouraged but may be used where advantageous for natural resource protection. 
(F)	Measures to promote filtration, percolation, and plant absorption of site run-off are preferred to minimize demand for centralized wet ponds. 
5.11.2.   Stormwater management features.
    In addition to bioretention swales and ditches, acceptable stormwater management devices include bioretention cells, retention and detention ponds, stormwater sewer pipes and box culverts, roadside gutters (valley gutters and gutters with standing or mountable curbs), perforated pipes, trench drains, and related inlet and discharge facilities. Common features appear below. The planning commission may approve other features. 

(A)	Bioretention features should be designed for two-year/twenty-four-hour storm events. Bioretention features should incorporate existing natural vegetation, where practical. 
(B)	Ponds, ditches, and swales should be cleared, grubbed and graded to function properly. Maintenance shelves shall be cleared of underbrush, but protected trees shall remain, where practical. 
(C)	Stormwater management features shall be protected as necessary from erosion with vegetation, rip-rap, or other stabilizing material. 
(D)	Pond banks shall be protected from erosion with vegetation or other stabilizing material which shall, at a minimum, be sod or hydroseed. Littoral vegetation to filter non-point-source pollution is preferred for the banks of wet ponds. Dry ponds shall be vegetated with sod or hydroseed, at a minimum. 
(E)	Land surrounding stormwater sewer pipes shall be cleared of underbrush, but protected trees shall remain and pipes shall be installed to minimize disturbance of tree root systems within required tree protection areas. 
(F)	Ditches and bioretention swales shall have a maximum side slope of 1:3 (three (3) feet of run per foot of rise) and a minimum flat-bottom width of two (2) feet. 
(G)	The bottoms of swales and ditches shall be at least one (1) foot above the water table to prevent stagnant water collection and allow for percolation. 
5.11.3.   Application of Berkeley County Standards.
(A)	Where practical, the proposed land development shall meet or exceed the requirements of the Berkeley County Stormwater Drainage Ordinance, as amended, and the "Berkeley County Engineering, Construction, and Development Standards Manual." 
(B)	The developer may choose to deviate from Berkeley County requirements with good cause, as determined by the planning commission, and in accordance with recognized professional engineering practices. The developer shall then propose alternative means of stormwater management and indicate to the planning commission how these means meet the intent of this ordinance, match or further reduce the risk of inundation from stormwater, and match or further reduce water pollution resulting from inundation and stormwater run-off, including erosion and sedimentation. 
5.11.4.   Application of state standards.
(A)	Where required by the South Carolina Codes and Regulations, the developer shall propose a plan that minimizes erosion and sedimentation during construction. The plan and its implementation shall meet or exceed the standards of the South Carolina Office of Ocean and Coastal Resources Management (OCRM), which has jurisdiction. The approved plans and letter denoting approval from OCRM shall be submitted to the city planner as part of an application for a land disturbance permit. 
(B)	Where applicable, the developer shall meet or exceed OCRM standards for stormwater management, which typically require that the proposed development provide for stormwater management that neither increases nor decreases existing stormwater run-off. The approved stormwater management plans and letter denoting approval from OCRM shall be submitted to the city planner as part of an application for a land disturbance permit. 
5.11.5.   Floodplain management standards.
(A)	The developer shall account for flood hazard areas that occur on the land proposed for development. It shall be the responsibility of the developer to locate boundaries of any floodplains delineated by the Federal Emergency Management Agency (FEMA) on the land and to indicate and label them in illustrations submitted during the land development review process. 
(B)	The proposed land development shall meet or exceed the standards of Hanahan City Code Chapter 5: Floodplain Damage Prevention Ordinance. 
(C)	Where practical, development shall be concentrated on land out of floodplains. Type "A" Planned Developments shall locate required open space in floodplains, where practical, to minimize intrusion. Type "B" Planned Developments shall be encouraged to achieve the same and to indicate so in its proposed master plan and text regulating development within the planned development district. 
(D)	Road standard related to flooding. The centerline elevation of proposed roads shall be above the ten-year floodplain. The planning commission may, however, modify this standard where necessary to prevent the filling of land resulting in loss of protected trees. 
5.12. - Water quality protection. 
5.12.1.   State and federal standards for wetlands protection and mitigation.
(A)	The developer shall survey land proposed for development and delineate wetlands where required by standards of S.C. Office of Ocean and Coastal Resources Management and/or U.S. Army Corps of Engineers. Delineated wetlands shall be indicated on the appropriate development plan submitted to the City of Hanahan for review. 
(B)	The developer shall indicate all measures required by S.C. OCRM and U.S. ACE to protect wetlands or mitigate impacts thereto on the same development plan. 
5.12.2.   Wetlands protection standards.
(A)	Where practical, the developer shall incorporate wetlands and any required wetland buffering, whether by local or state standards, into commonly owned property and not into numerous individually owned lots. 
(B)	Maintenance shall be provided per Section 4.5. Deed restrictions restricting the disturbance and encroachment of wetlands and associated buffers shall be stated on each plat of a parcel containing these features. 
(C)	Rear yard setbacks shall be measured from the highland edge of the wetland buffer, where provided, to prevent encroachment by construction activity. 

5.12.3.   Goose Creek Reservoir Protection.
(A)	A major land development shall designate all land within thirty-five (35) feet of the OCRM-recognized critical line of the Goose Creek Reservoir as a wetland buffer to protect the water quality of the reservoir. State standards may require a deeper buffer. The buffer shall be indicated on the preliminary land development plan. 
(B)	Site redevelopment next to the reservoir. For a major land development proposed on an existing developed site cleared of vegetation, the proposed preliminary land development plan for redevelopment or expansion of the existing development shall propose planting the buffer. 
(1)	The planted buffer shall consist of six (6) canopy trees and thirty-five (35) shrubs per one hundred (100) linear feet, and natural groundcover to inhibit erosion, slow sheet run-off, and encourage permeation of run-off into the ground. 
(2)	The planning commission may modify this standard, where it deems necessary to ensure quality redevelopment that furthers the objectives of this ordinance, modernizes stormwater management, remedies site contamination, and takes alternative steps to mitigate water pollution. 
5.12.4.   Buffer design standards.
(A)	Pre-existing natural vegetation in buffers required by the City of Hanahan shall be preserved. These areas promote filtration of stormwater run-off, which inhibits non-point-source water pollution entering the Goose Creek Reservoir or other protected wetland. 
(B)	Disturbances shall be limited to routine maintenance to remove noxious weeds, invasive species, and litter, to prune trees and undergrowth, and to plant supplemental vegetation, if desired, to improve the buffer aesthetically or functionally. 
(C)	Encroachments into the buffer shall be limited to approved view corridors, which may access docks, and infrastructure that crosses the buffer and wetland, as approved by applicable county, state, and federal authorities as well as the City of Hanahan. 
(D)	View corridors up to twenty (20) feet wide may be cut through the buffer to afford views of wetlands. The corridor shall be cut on an angle of at least thirty (30) degrees relative to the general orientation of the critical line across the parcel to prevent channeling of stormwater run-off in the corridor. The cleared area shall be stabilized with grass, mulch, or other vegetative materials to prevent erosion and sedimentation of the wetland. Docks, where approved by applicable state and federal authorities, may be installed in the view corridor. 
(E)	Trees throughout the buffer may be limbed up, but no higher than one-third ( 1/3 ) of the height of the tree. The removal of lower limbs affords property owners views of the wetland between the trees. Shrubs and other low-lying vegetation may be pruned down to four (4) feet, provided no more than one-third ( 1/3 ) of each shrub is removed, to allow views as well. 
5.12.5.   Buffer design standards for recreational access.

    Buffers fifty (50) feet or more in depth provided voluntarily may be encroached by pervious walkways. 
(A)	Clearing and grubbing of vegetation and grading for the walkway shall be limited to the width of the walkway plus three (3) feet on both sides for shoulders. Twenty (20) feet shall be the maximum allowable width cleared and graded for the walkway. 
(B)	The shoulders of the walkway shall be revegetated, mulched, or otherwise stabilized to prevent erosion. 
(C)	The walkway shall be a pervious surface, including but not limited to a boardwalk with spaced boards, which may be raised for brief wetland crossings, where approved by appropriate state and federal authorities. 
5.13. - Green space. 
5.13.1.   Open space.

    Unencumbered, buildable land prior to proposed land development that is required for or otherwise committed to stormwater management, non-jurisdictional wetlands, wetland buffering, natural and cultural resource conservation, and landscaped common areas, shall be considered open space for purposes of this ordinance and the Hanahan Zoning Ordinance, which may encourage or require open space conservation for land development approval. Wetlands required to be preserved by other entities, including tidal marsh and the Goose Creek Reservoir, shall not be considered open space for these purposes. Land occupied by structures and vehicle circulation and parking is not open space. 
5.13.2.   Park space.

    Unencumbered, buildable land prior to proposed land development that is programmed for passive or active recreation and leisure shall be considered park space for the purposes of this ordinance and the Hanahan Zoning Ordinance, which may encourage or require provision of park space for land development approval. 
(A)	Park space shall include, at a minimum, one (1) of the following two (2) elements: 
(1)	A well-defined trail system for pedestrian access throughout the area indicated as park space, which may include dense vegetation or an open field; or 
(2)	An easily accessible open lawn passable by pedestrians throughout. The lawn may include shade trees, ornamental plantings, flowerbeds, park furniture, public art, and other outdoor amenities. 
(B)	Park space shall include a program for regular maintenance, including mowing, pruning, weeding, mulching, repaving, replanting, and irrigation, as needed to maintain the intended appearance and accessibility. 
(C)	Recreational wetland buffers, standards for which appear above, subsection 5.12.5, shall be considered park space. Other wetlands buffers shall be considered open space. 
(D)	Wet and dry stormwater management ponds shall be considered park space when they are incorporated into a pedestrian circulation system and utilized as an aesthetic design feature. Ponds located to the rear of structures shall typically be considered open space. 
(E)	Wetlands, including tidal marsh and the Goose Creek Reservoir shall not be considered park space for the purpose of land development review. 
(F)	For the purposes of the Hanahan Zoning and Land Development ordinances, park space is neither occupied by fully enclosed structures nor programmed for vehicle circulation and parking; however, adequate parking and facilities, such as restrooms, may be required or encouraged. 
5.14. - Potable water. 
(A)	Access to potable water. The developer shall demonstrate that each buildable lot within the proposed land development shall be provided access to potable water. The means of potable water provision shall meet or exceed the standards of the South Carolina Department of Health and Environmental Control and the water service provider, where applicable, from which service is desired. 
(1)	The developer proposing a land development within five hundred (500) feet of a public water system shall extend the water system to the land development, if acceptable to the public water service provider. The developer shall then extend the public water supply system to each buildable lot in the land development. 
(2)	On-site water supply. The developer not required to extend public water system to a proposed land development may choose on-site water supply. This developer shall demonstrate that each proposed buildable lot can be served by a private on-site system. The developer shall make that system available prior to transferring the lot or shall make the installation of the system prior to issuance of a building permit a condition of sale for each lot. This condition shall be noted on the deed to the property transferred. 
(B)	Access to water for fire protection. The developer proposing extension of the public water supply system shall install fire hydrants as required by building and fire codes, as adopted by the City of Hanahan. 
5.15. - Sanitary sewerage. 
(A)	Ability to dispose of sewerage. The developer shall demonstrate that each buildable lot within the proposed land development shall be provided direct access to sanitary sewerage along the road frontage of the parcel or have the capacity - including soils and environmental conditions - required for an on-site disposal system. The means of sewage disposal shall meet or exceed the standards of the South Carolina Department of Health and Environmental Control and the sanitary sewer service provider, where applicable, from which service is desired. 
(1)	The developer shall connect to sanitary sewerage as required by the Berkeley-Charleston-Dorchester Council of Governments under its regional water quality management plan. 
(2)	Where proposed to serve the land development, the sanitary sewer system shall be extended to each buildable lot in the proposed land development. The extension shall meet or exceed the standards of the service provider for inclusion in the sanitary sewer system as public infrastructure. 
(3)	Where connection to sanitary sewerage is not required or desired, the developer shall demonstrate that each buildable lot has the capacity to accommodate an on-site disposal system. 
(B)	Property redevelopment. A parcel proposed for development with an existing on-site disposal system shall demonstrate, where the redevelopment triggers compliance with this ordinance, that the system is functioning properly. Routine maintenance shall be performed on the system prior to the issuance of a zoning permit for the property served. In the event that the system is found deficient, the applicant for a zoning permit shall rectify the condition by repairing or replacing the system or connecting to a sanitary sewer system. 
(C)	Pump station. Where needed to adequately serve the land development, as determined by the service provider, the developer may include a pump station on a remnant parcel of land adjacent to a transportation right-of-way or ingress/egress easement. The pump station shall be readily accessible to utility staff but shall be located, to the extent practical, in an unobtrusive location away from areas of potentially heavy pedestrian traffic and away from the primary entrances of non-residential structures open to the public. 
5.16. - Other utilities. 
(A)	Electrical power. The developer shall demonstrate that each buildable lot within the proposed land development shall be provided access to electricity via written notice from the proposed provider that describes means of access and point of entry into the existing system. The means of electrical power provision shall meet or exceed the standards of the proposed service provider. 
(B)	Natural gas, telephone, television, and internet access. The developer who proposes natural gas, telephone, television, and internet access via pipeline, wire, and cable, as applicable, shall meet or exceed the requirements of the service provider. 
(C)	Utility lines. 
(1)	All utility lines proposed in a major land development shall be located underground and parallel to roads, except as necessary to cross bridges, connect to existing above-ground lines, and connect structures served. The lines and related equipment shall be readily accessible to utility staff. 
(2)	Utility lines shall be collected in easements or rights-of-way, to the extent practical, to use land more efficiently and to minimize disruption to and loss of natural vegetation. 
(D)	Utility equipment location. Equipment related to the transmission of the utility shall be located in discreet locations to the extent practical, such as lot corners. The developer shall ensure that equipment is in no danger of inundation from stormwater and shall not locate equipment in or too near drainage facilities. 
(E)	Major transmission. The standards of this section are intended for the developer installing service within a proposed land development. Major transmission lines and related equipment may be designed and constructed to meet the needs of the utility provider. The proposal shall not violate the objectives of this ordinance. 
5.17. - Rights-of-way and easements. 
5.17.1.   General standards.
(A)	All public improvements shall be incorporated into an easement or right-of-way dedicated to perpetual public use and assigned to an entity responsible for its maintenance per Section 4.5. This shall be noted on the final plat and any record drawing illustrating public improvements. 
(B)	Easements and rights-of-way shall be of such dimensions to incorporate the public improvements, including shoulders and banks, and to provide sufficient access for adequate maintenance of the improvements. 
5.17.2.   Roads and driveways.
(A)	All improvements intended for the traveling public shall be incorporated into a transportation right-of-way dedicated to S.C. Department of Transportation, Berkeley County, or a property owners association, representative of all properties reliant upon the improvements for access, established for the purposes of owning and maintaining the improvements. Exceptions shall be as follows: 
(1)	Land intended for the expansion of a pre-existing road and right-of-way shall be reserved as an easement dedicated for that purpose. Land intended for the future extension of an existing or proposed road and right-of-way shall be reserved as an easement dedicated for that purpose. Once constructed, the improvements may be dedicated and incorporated into a transportation right-of-way. 
(2)	Two (2) neighboring lots with one (1) primary structure each may share a driveway within an ingress/egress easement. The easement shall be centered along the common lot line with a width equal to the width of the driveway and any provided sidewalks plus two (2) feet, minimum, on both sides. 
(3)	Internal circulation roads in attached-unit residential community shall be incorporated into easements dedicated for perpetual access to the traveling public, except where rights-of-way are provided. A property owners association representative of all properties reliant upon the improvements for access shall be charged with responsibility for maintenance of these internal circulation roads. The easements shall occur on land owned by the same. 
(4)	Access management. The planning commission may encourage or the S.C. Department of Transportation or Berkeley County may require the developer of a large land development to implement "access management." The purpose is to coordinate the access to the public right-of-way from multiple parcels in a land development to reduce vehicular conflict points in the right-of-way. 
(a)	To accomplish access management, internal circulation roads in land developments shall be incorporated into easements dedicated for perpetual access to the traveling public, except where rights-of-way are provided. The improvements in the easement shall be maintained by the largest landowner relying on access, such as the anchor of a commercial land development, or by a property owners association representative of all properties reliant upon the improvements for access. 
(b)	Each parcel with frontage on the public right-of-way shall nevertheless provide pedestrian access directly to and along that right-of-way. 
(B)	No property shall be proposed to be solely reliant on an ingress-egress easement for access, except as provided for access management. 
(C)	An ingress-egress easement incorporating a road shall not encroach a required yard. Setbacks required by zoning district shall be measured from the boundaries of the ingress-egress easement. 
5.17.3.   Pedestrian facilities.
(A)	Sidewalks shall be incorporated into adjacent road right-of-way, where practical. 
(B)	Other walkways may be incorporated into easements or rights-of-way. Clear provisions for ownership and maintenance shall be provided. 
5.17.4.   Drainage.
(A)	Natural drainage courses as well as tidal marsh (saltwater wetlands) under the control of the State of South Carolina shall be incorporated into rights-of-way. 
(B)	Stormwater management features that discharge into or otherwise utilize freshwater wetlands in stormwater management plans shall be incorporated into a drainage easement, if they are not incorporated into a natural drainage course right-of-way. 
(C)	All artificial drainage improvements shall be incorporated into easements or rights-of-way adequate in width and condition to accommodate the improvements and allow for access for maintenance. 
(D)	Drainage easements shall be centered along lot boundaries where practical. Drainage easements may be located in required yards. Encroachment of drainage easements into building envelopes shall be minimized to the greatest extent practical. 
5.17.5.   Water and sewer.
(A)	Water and sewer improvements shall be generally located in rights-of-way or easements adequate in width and condition to accommodate the improvements and allow for access for maintenance. Improvements proposed for dedication to public utilities shall meet or exceed the standards thereof. 
(B)	Easements for water and sewer improvements shall be centered along lot boundaries where practical. Such easements may be located in required yards. Encroachment of water and sewer easements into building envelopes shall be minimized to the greatest extent practical. 
5.17.6.   Other utilities.
(A)	Utilities not specified above, including but not limited to telephone, electricity, and television, shall be located in rights-of-way or easements adequate in width and condition to accommodate the improvements and allow for access for maintenance. 
(B)	Easements shall collocate where practical to minimize encroachment into building envelopes and natural resources. 
5.18. - Adequate, oversized, and off-site improvements. 
(A)	Improvements shall be designed and constructed to serve all current and future phases of the major land development and the planned development district, as applicable. 
(B)	Oversized improvements. The planning commission may require the developer to install capital improvements adequate in size and capacity to serve future development on nearby land where the service provider determines that such improvements are needed to adequately serve future development in the vicinity of the proposed development. 
(1)	Oversized improvements required during development review. The developer shall be notified of the need for oversized improvements prior to approval of the preliminary land development plan, and the requirement shall not delay the development review timeline. The service provider (City of Hanahan, Berkeley County, or other) shall verify the need for oversized improvements and shall commit to accepting and maintaining the improvements upon completion. 
(2)	Infrastructure system connectivity. Road stubs and other improvements designed to ensure interconnected systems of infrastructure in Hanahan shall not be considered oversized improvements and shall be considered basic requirements for proposed improvements. 
(3)	Cost sharing. The developer shall be responsible only for costs associated with improvements needed to serve his development, including future phases and the Planned Development District. The developer shall install oversized improvements required by the planning commission. The service provider shall provide the materials and reimburse the developer for expenses incurred. The service provider and the developer may enter into a voluntary alternative arrangement achieving the goal of complete systems of infrastructure. 
(C)	Off-site improvements. The developer shall be responsible for all capital improvements to existing systems of infrastructure to which the development proposes to connect. 
(1)	The developer shall perform any studies needed (e.g., traffic study) to determine what improvements to systems will be necessitated by the proposed development. The study may be reviewed or performed by the service provider, if it accepts the responsibility, or an independent third party qualified to review or perform the study. 
(2)	The developer shall fully implement improvements that the study concludes are necessitated by the proposed development. 
(3)	The planning commission may require that off-site improvements also be oversized to serve future development outside the proposed Land Development or Planned Development District, in which case oversized improvements standards (above) shall apply. 
(D)	Limitations on city requirements. 
(1)	The City of Hanahan shall not require a developer to rectify pre-existing inadequate levels of service that are unrelated to, or out of scale and proportion with, the proposed land development and expected impacts thereof. The developer shall only be responsible to offset impacts reasonably expected from his proposal at build-out. 
(2)	The developer shall not be required to fund or provide equipment, maintenance, personnel, or other operating costs for public infrastructure or service providers.
